================================================================================
  RECALL JS.1 â€” Project Nornyx / Project Zeus
  Complete change manifest for all UI, backend, and routing modifications
  recorded from the original codebase state.

  PURPOSE:
    Any AI system or developer can read this document and reproduce every
    change listed here, in order, from scratch, on a clean copy of the
    original codebase. Changes are grouped by feature, not by file, so
    context and intent are preserved alongside the implementation details.

  SCOPE:
    All changes made across all sessions up to March 31, 2026.
    "Original" means the codebase before any of these sessions began.

  TECH STACK:
    - SvelteKit with Svelte 5 rune syntax ($props, $state, $derived, $effect)
    - TypeScript throughout
    - Drizzle ORM with SQLite (libsql / Turso)
    - PartyKit for real-time multiplayer socket messaging
    - Vite + svelte-kit/adapter-vercel
    - Path aliases: $lib â†’ src/lib, $components â†’ src/lib/components,
      $stores â†’ src/lib/stores, $server â†’ src/lib/server, $types â†’ src/lib/types

  ROUTING CONVENTION:
    - All routes live under  site/src/routes/
    - Dynamic segments use [id] bracket syntax (SvelteKit file-based routing)
    - +page.server.ts  = server-only load function (runs on server before render)
    - +page.svelte     = page component (runs on both server and client)
    - +server.ts       = API endpoint (no page, pure JSON responses)
    - +layout.svelte   = layout wrapper (NOT modified in these sessions)

  FILE PATH FORMAT:
    All paths in this document are relative to  project-zeus/site/src/
    unless prefixed with  project-zeus/  for project-level files.

  SVELTE 5 RUNE SYNTAX NOTES:
    - let { x } = $props()         â€” declare component props
    - let x = $state(initial)      â€” reactive state variable
    - let x = $derived(expr)       â€” computed value, re-runs when deps change
    - let x = $derived.by(() => {}) â€” computed with function body
    - $effect(() => {})            â€” side effect, re-runs when deps change
    - $effect returns a cleanup fn if needed (return () => cleanup())

================================================================================


================================================================================
  GROUP 1 â€” FOUC PREVENTION & THEME FLASH FIX
  Purpose: Apply the user's saved theme BEFORE the first browser paint so
           there is never a flash of wrong-theme or unstyled content (FOUC).
  Files modified: site/src/app.html
================================================================================

CHANGE 1.1 â€” Add visibility:hidden guard on <html> until theme is applied
  File: app.html
  Location: Inside <head>, immediately before the blocking theme script.

  Add this <style> tag as the FIRST thing after the <link> tags in <head>:

      <style>html:not(.fouc-ready) { visibility: hidden; }</style>

  Explanation:
    This CSS hides the entire page until the class "fouc-ready" is added to
    <html>. The hidden state lasts only microseconds â€” the blocking IIFE
    below adds the class synchronously. The result: the user never sees
    unstyled content, a white flash, or the wrong theme on page load or
    navigation. This is a pure CSS guard; it does not rely on JavaScript
    executing â€” if JS is disabled the page will remain invisible, which is
    acceptable because this app requires JS.

CHANGE 1.2 â€” Add blocking IIFE script to restore saved theme before first paint
  File: app.html
  Location: Inside <head>, immediately after the visibility:hidden <style>.

  Add this <script> block (must be a plain IIFE â€” no type="module", no
  async/defer â€” so browsers execute it synchronously before rendering):

      <script>
          (function () {
              var VALID = [
                  'arcane-celestial',
                  'dark-academia',
                  'void-astral',
                  'silver-scroll',
                  'forge-iron',
                  'morning-mist',
                  'midnight-court',
                  'clean-slate',
                  'blood-oath',
                  'vellum-quill',
                  'sakura-court',
                  'frozen-spire'
              ];
              try {
                  var saved = localStorage.getItem('nornyx-theme');
                  if (saved && VALID.indexOf(saved) !== -1) {
                      document.documentElement.dataset.theme = saved;
                  }
              } catch (e) {
                  // localStorage unavailable (private browsing, security policy)
                  // Fall through â€” default theme is used silently.
              }
              // CRITICAL: classList.add must be OUTSIDE the try/catch block.
              // If localStorage throws, we must still reveal the page â€”
              // otherwise the page stays invisible forever.
              document.documentElement.classList.add('fouc-ready');
          })();
      </script>

  How it works:
    1. The IIFE runs synchronously before the browser paints anything.
    2. It validates the saved theme string against the VALID list â€”
       never trusting arbitrary localStorage content.
    3. It sets data-theme on <html>, which activates the matching
       CSS [data-theme='...'] block (defined in app.css).
    4. It adds the class "fouc-ready" to <html> (outside try/catch),
       which satisfies the html:not(.fouc-ready) guard and makes the
       page visible.
    5. On first visit (no saved theme), no data-theme is set and the
       CSS :root defaults (arcane-celestial) are used.

CHANGE 1.3 â€” Complete app.html head structure with all font families
  File: app.html
  Location: <head>, before the FOUC script.

  The <link> tag below loads all 14 font families used across all 12 themes
  in a single HTTP request. Preconnect links reduce DNS + TLS negotiation
  time. The display=swap parameter prevents invisible text during load.

      <link rel="preconnect" href="https://fonts.googleapis.com" />
      <link rel="preconnect" href="https://fonts.gstatic.com" crossorigin="anonymous" />
      <link
          rel="stylesheet"
          href="https://fonts.googleapis.com/css2?family=Arvo:wght@400;600&family=Cinzel+Decorative:wght@400;700&family=Cinzel:wght@400;600;700&family=Crimson+Pro:wght@400;600&family=IM+Fell+English&family=Lora:wght@400;600&family=Nunito:wght@400;600;700&family=Orbitron:wght@400;600;700&family=Playfair+Display:wght@600;700&family=Rajdhani:wght@400;600&family=Rye&family=Space+Grotesk:wght@400;600;700&family=Spectral:wght@400;600&family=Uncial+Antiqua&display=swap"
      />

  Font-to-theme mapping:
    Cinzel / Cinzel Decorative â€” arcane-celestial, silver-scroll, blood-oath,
                                  forge-iron (display), nav brand text
    Rye                        â€” dark-academia (Dusty Trail) display
    Arvo                       â€” dark-academia (Dusty Trail) UI
    Space Grotesk              â€” void-astral display + UI
    Orbitron                   â€” clean-slate (Forged Steel) display
    Rajdhani                   â€” clean-slate (Forged Steel) UI
    Playfair Display           â€” midnight-court display
    Lora                       â€” sakura-court display
    Uncial Antiqua             â€” morning-mist (Grove Circle) display
    Nunito                     â€” morning-mist (Grove Circle) UI
    Spectral                   â€” forge-iron (Ashen Gate) UI, blood-oath UI
    IM Fell English            â€” vellum-quill display
    Crimson Pro                â€” vellum-quill UI

  GROUP 2 â€” DESIGN TOKENS & GLOBAL CSS (app.css)
  Purpose: A complete set of CSS custom properties (design tokens) that every
           component uses instead of hardcoded colour values. 12 theme
           overrides. Global badge, button, layout, and utility classes.
  Files modified: app.css
================================================================================

CHANGE 2.1 â€” :root design token block
  File: app.css
  Replace / set the entire :root block with:

      :root {
          --bg: #07111f;
          --bg-alt: #0d1b2f;
          --surface: rgba(15, 28, 48, 0.88);
          --border: rgba(120, 164, 255, 0.2);
          --text: #edf3ff;
          --text-muted: #9db2d1;
          --accent: #7c9cff;
          --accent-2: #34d3a2;
          --danger: #ff6d8a;
          --warning: #ffd36b;
          --shadow: 0 22px 60px rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.35);
          --radius: 18px;
          --radius-lg: 24px;

          /* Extended tokens â€” components use these instead of hardcoded values */
          --nav-bg: rgba(7, 17, 31, 0.85);
          --toast-bg: rgba(15, 28, 48, 0.95);
          --toast-bg-hover: rgba(20, 36, 60, 0.97);
          --quest-accent: #c084fc;
          --orb-3-color: #a855f7;
          --card-hover-border: rgba(124, 156, 255, 0.4);
          --blur-glass: 18px;
          --body-gradient: radial-gradient(circle at top, rgba(124, 156, 255, 0.18), transparent 30%),
              linear-gradient(180deg, #091220 0%, #040912 100%);

          --font-display: 'Cinzel', serif;
          --font-ui: Inter, 'Segoe UI', system-ui, sans-serif;
      }

  Token reference:
    --bg              Page background colour
    --bg-alt          Slightly lighter bg for nested surfaces (popovers, etc.)
    --surface         Card/panel glass surface (semi-opaque)
    --border          Border colour for all panels, inputs, cards
    --text            Primary body text
    --text-muted      Secondary / label text
    --accent          Primary interactive accent (links, active states, focus rings)
    --accent-2        Secondary accent (success badges, glow effects)
    --danger          Error / delete / dangerous action colour
    --warning         Warning / lobby / pending state colour
    --shadow          Box shadow used by GlassPanel and elevated elements
    --radius          Default border-radius for cards, buttons, inputs
    --radius-lg       Larger radius for modals, popovers
    --nav-bg          Navigation bar background (semi-opaque)
    --toast-bg        Toast notification background
    --toast-bg-hover  Toast hover state background
    --quest-accent     Quest panel accent colour
    --orb-3-color      Third decorative orb colour (hero/landing page)
    --card-hover-border Card border colour on hover
    --blur-glass       backdrop-filter blur value for glass panels
    --body-gradient    Full-page background gradient
    --font-display     Thematic display/heading font
    --font-ui          UI/body font

CHANGE 2.4 â€” Frozen Spire badge contrast overrides
  File: app.css
  Location: After the frozen-spire [data-theme] block.

  frozen-spire is a light theme. The default badge colours are designed for
  dark backgrounds and would be illegible or invisible on the light bg.
  These overrides replace the glow with a dark blue equivalent.

      [data-theme='frozen-spire'] .badge-active {
          background: rgba(26, 92, 168, 0.12);
          color: #1a5ca8;
          text-shadow: 0 0 10px rgba(26, 92, 168, 0.55);
          box-shadow: 0 0 8px rgba(26, 92, 168, 0.12);
      }

      [data-theme='frozen-spire'] .badge-multiplayer {
          background: rgba(26, 92, 168, 0.12);
          color: #1a5ca8;
      }

CHANGE 2.5 â€” Global reset, layout, button, form control, and utility classes
  File: app.css
  Location: After all [data-theme] blocks and badge rules.

  These rules form the global baseline for the entire application. They are
  written once and inherit CSS custom properties from the theme tokens above,
  so they automatically adapt to all 12 themes without change.

      let activeEmblem = $state(0);

CHANGE 3.2 â€” 3-zone flex layout
  File: lib/components/Nav.svelte

  The nav bar is a sticky strip divided into three horizontal zones:

      Zone 1 (left):  .nav-brand â€” logo + "Project Nornyx" text, flex-shrink: 0
      Zone 2 (center): .nav-links â€” horizontal page links, flex: 1, justify-content: center
      Zone 3 (right): .nav-right â€” ThemePicker + user/auth buttons + hamburger, flex-shrink: 0

  The .nav-inner container:

      .nav-inner {

  Nav links shown in Zone 2: Home, About, Reviews, Adventures (only when logged in).
  Active link styling: color: var(--accent) + background: color-mix(in srgb, var(--accent) 10%, transparent).

  It renders a trigger button (coloured dot + "Theme" label) and a popover

================================================================================
  GROUP 4 â€” ACTIVE ADVENTURE PAGE FIXES
  Purpose: Fix three bugs present in the original adventure page:
           1. Main-page scrollbar visible alongside overflow-locked body
           2. Scroll-to-bottom animation firing on initial load (jarring)
           3. Flash of CharacterCreation screen before data hydrates
           Plus one visual fix: inter-panel glow/shadow effect
  Files modified: routes/adventures/[id]/+page.svelte
================================================================================

CHANGE 4.1 â€” Lock html overflow as well as body
  File: routes/adventures/[id]/+page.svelte

  ORIGINAL CODE (in an $effect that locks scrolling when the page mounts):

      document.body.style.overflow = 'hidden';
      return () => { document.body.style.overflow = ''; };

  CHANGED TO:

      document.documentElement.style.overflow = 'hidden';
      document.body.style.overflow = 'hidden';
      return () => {
          document.documentElement.style.overflow = '';
          document.body.style.overflow = '';
      };

  Why: Locking only <body> leaves <html> scrollable in some browsers,
  causing a visible second scrollbar on the main page. Locking both
  elements eliminates it completely.

CHANGE 4.2 â€” Parametrize scrollChatToBottom + call with 'instant' on mount
  File: routes/adventures/[id]/+page.svelte

  ORIGINAL function signature:

      function scrollChatToBottom() {

  CHANGED TO:

      function scrollChatToBottom(behavior: ScrollBehavior = 'smooth') {

  And wherever the function performs the scroll, pass behavior through:

      el.scrollTo({ top: el.scrollHeight, behavior });

  In onMount, change the call from:

      scrollChatToBottom();

  TO:

      scrollChatToBottom('instant');

  Why: On initial page load, animating the scroll to the bottom of a
  potentially long transcript looks unpolished and causes layout shift.
  Using 'instant' on mount snaps to the bottom immediately. Subsequent
  scrolls (new messages arriving) continue to use 'smooth' by default.

CHANGE 4.3 â€” Initialize partyCharacters from server data synchronously
  File: routes/adventures/[id]/+page.svelte

  ORIGINAL declaration:

      let partyCharacters = $state<Record<string, PlayerCharacter>>({});

  CHANGED TO:

      let partyCharacters = $state<Record<string, PlayerCharacter>>(
          Object.fromEntries(
              (((data.gameState as { characters?: PlayerCharacter[] } | undefined)
                  ?.characters ?? []) as PlayerCharacter[])
                  .map((character) => [character.userId, character])
          )
      );

  Why: With the original empty-object initialization, the $derived
  "currentCharacter" resolved to null on the first render, causing the
  CharacterCreation screen to flash briefly before the $effect that
  populated partyCharacters from socket data ran. By initializing
  directly from data.gameState.characters (which is available
  synchronously from the server load), currentCharacter is never null
  on first render for returning players.

CHANGE 4.4 â€” Remove inter-panel shadow darkening
  File: routes/adventures/[id]/+page.svelte

  The .adventure-screen rule is the primary layout container for the entire
  active adventure page. It already existed with a full CSS grid layout;
  the property --shadow: none was ADDED as the final line inside that existing
  rule. An implementer must write (or preserve) the complete block:

      .adventure-screen {
          height: calc(100dvh - 3.5rem);
          display: grid;
          grid-template-columns: 240px minmax(0, 1fr) 460px;
          grid-template-rows: auto 1fr;
          grid-template-areas:
              "header header journal"
              "left   main   journal";
          column-gap: 0.85rem;
          row-gap: 0;
          padding: 0.3rem 0 1.5rem;
          overflow: hidden;
          --shadow: none;     /* â† THE ADDED LINE */
      }

  Layout explained:
    - height: calc(100dvh - 3.5rem) â€” fills the full viewport minus nav height;
      dvh (dynamic viewport height) avoids the mobile address-bar jump.
    - grid-template-columns: 240px left sidebar | flexible main content | 460px journal
    - grid-template-areas: the header row spans both left + main columns;
      the journal panel spans both rows (tall single column on the right).
    - overflow: hidden â€” each panel manages its own internal scrolling;
      no page-level scroll occurs inside the adventure screen.
    - --shadow: none â€” the ONLY property added in this change. It is
      inherited by every child GlassPanel via the CSS cascade. The default
      --shadow value produces a glow/darkening ring between adjacent panels;
      setting it to none on the parent removes the effect simultaneously for
      all child panels without modifying the component or global CSS.

  Why: The default --shadow creates an uneven darkening effect between the
  sidebar, main content area, and journal panel. Overriding it at the
  container level is the minimal surgical fix â€” it does not affect the
  summary page or any other route that uses GlassPanel.


================================================================================
  GROUP 5 â€” ADVENTURE LIFECYCLE API ENDPOINT
  Purpose: Allow the adventure owner to mark an adventure as "completed"
           or permanently delete it via REST API calls.
  Files created: routes/api/adventure/[id]/+server.ts  (NEW FILE)
================================================================================

CHANGE 5.1 â€” Create /api/adventure/[id]/+server.ts
  This file is created from scratch. Full file content:

      import { json, error } from '@sveltejs/kit';
      import type { RequestHandler } from './$types';
      import { db } from '$server/db/client';
      import {
          adventures,
          adventureMembers,
          adventureState,
          adventureChat,
          adventureTurns
      } from '$server/db/schema';
      import { eq, and } from 'drizzle-orm';

      /**
       * PATCH /api/adventure/[id]
       * Body: { status: 'completed' }
       * Owner-only. Marks an adventure as completed.
       */
      export const PATCH: RequestHandler = async ({ params, locals, request }) => {
          if (!locals.user) error(401, 'Not authenticated');

          const { id: adventureId } = params;

          const [adv] = await db
              .select({ id: adventures.id, ownerId: adventures.ownerId })
              .from(adventures)
              .where(and(eq(adventures.id, adventureId), eq(adventures.ownerId, locals.user.id)))
              .limit(1);

          if (!adv) error(404, 'Adventure not found or not owner');

          const body = (await request.json().catch(() => ({}))) as { status?: string };
          if (body.status !== 'completed') error(400, 'Only status: completed is accepted');

          await db
              .update(adventures)
              .set({ status: 'completed', updatedAt: Date.now() })
              .where(eq(adventures.id, adventureId));

          return json({ ok: true });
      };

      /**
       * DELETE /api/adventure/[id]
       * Owner-only. Permanently deletes an adventure and all its data.
       * Child rows are deleted in FK dependency order.
       */
      export const DELETE: RequestHandler = async ({ params, locals }) => {
          if (!locals.user) error(401, 'Not authenticated');

          const { id: adventureId } = params;

          const [adv] = await db
              .select({ id: adventures.id, ownerId: adventures.ownerId })
              .from(adventures)
              .where(and(eq(adventures.id, adventureId), eq(adventures.ownerId, locals.user.id)))
              .limit(1);

          if (!adv) error(404, 'Adventure not found or not owner');

          // Delete in FK dependency order: children before parent
          await db.delete(adventureChat).where(eq(adventureChat.adventureId, adventureId));
          await db.delete(adventureTurns).where(eq(adventureTurns.adventureId, adventureId));
          await db.delete(adventureState).where(eq(adventureState.adventureId, adventureId));
          await db.delete(adventureMembers).where(eq(adventureMembers.adventureId, adventureId));
          await db.delete(adventures).where(eq(adventures.id, adventureId));

          return json({ ok: true });
      };

  Security notes:
    - Both handlers require locals.user (auth guard) â€” unauthenticated
      calls get 401 immediately.
    - Both handlers verify ownerId === locals.user.id before touching any
      data â€” non-owners get 404 (not 403, to avoid leaking existence).
    - PATCH only accepts status='completed' â€” any other body is rejected
      with 400 to prevent arbitrary status mutation.
    - DELETE order matters â€” adventureChat first, then adventureTurns,
      then adventureState, then adventureMembers, then adventures. Reversing
      this order will violate foreign key constraints.

CHANGE 6.2 â€” Add management state variables and handlers
  File: lib/components/AdventureCard.svelte

  Add to the <script> section:

      let busy = $state(false);
      let confirmingDelete = $state(false);
      let errorMsg = $state('');

      async function handleComplete() {
          if (busy) return;
          busy = true;
          errorMsg = '';
          try {
              const res = await fetch(`/api/adventure/${adventure.id}`, {
                  method: 'PATCH',
                  headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' },
                  body: JSON.stringify({ status: 'completed' })
              });
              if (!res.ok) throw new Error(await res.text());
              onAction();
          } catch (e) {
              errorMsg = 'Failed to complete adventure.';
          } finally {
              busy = false;
          }
      }

      async function handleDelete() {
          if (busy) return;
          busy = true;
          errorMsg = '';
          try {
              const res = await fetch(`/api/adventure/${adventure.id}`, { method: 'DELETE' });
              if (!res.ok) throw new Error(await res.text());
              onAction();
          } catch (e) {
              errorMsg = 'Failed to delete adventure.';
          } finally {
              busy = false;
              confirmingDelete = false;
          }
      }

    wants to interact with them.

  GROUP 8 â€” COMPLETED ADVENTURE SUMMARY ROUTE
  Purpose: When a user navigates to /adventures/[id] on a completed adventure,
           redirect them to /adventures/[id]/summary â€” a dedicated read-only
           chronicle page showing the full transcript, stats, party snapshot,
           quest log, world map, and NPC roster.
  Files created: routes/adventures/[id]/summary/+page.server.ts  (NEW FILE)
                 routes/adventures/[id]/summary/+page.svelte      (NEW FILE)
  Files modified: routes/adventures/[id]/+page.server.ts

CHANGE 8.1 â€” Add completed redirect in [id]/+page.server.ts
  File: routes/adventures/[id]/+page.server.ts

  Location: After the existing lobby redirect (status === 'lobby' â†’ /lobby).

  ADD these lines immediately after the lobby redirect:

      // Completed adventures have their own summary view
      if (adventure[0].status === 'completed') {
          redirect(302, `/adventures/${params.id}/summary`);
      }

  Why: Without this, a direct URL visit to /adventures/[id] on a completed
  adventure would try to render the active adventure page (with socket
  connection, combat UI, chat input, etc.) for a finished story. The summary
  route renders a read-only chronicle instead.

CHANGE 8.2 â€” Create summary/+page.server.ts
  File: routes/adventures/[id]/summary/+page.server.ts  (NEW FILE)

  This file is the server-side load function for the completed adventure
  summary page. Full content:

      import { redirect, error } from '@sveltejs/kit';
      import type { PageServerLoad } from './$types';
      import { db } from '$server/db/client';
      import {
          adventures, adventureMembers, adventureState,
          adventureTurns, adventureChat, users
      } from '$server/db/schema';
      import { eq, and, asc } from 'drizzle-orm';
      import { createInitialGameState, migrateState } from '$lib/game/state';
      import type { TurnRecord, StateChange } from '$lib/game/types';

      export const load: PageServerLoad = async ({ params, locals, url }) => {
          if (!locals.user) {
              redirect(302, `/auth/login?returnTo=${encodeURIComponent(url.pathname + url.search)}`);
          }

          const [adv] = await db
              .select()
              .from(adventures)
              .where(eq(adventures.id, params.id))
              .limit(1);

          if (!adv) error(404, 'Adventure not found');

          // Guard: redirect away if not actually completed
          if (adv.status === 'lobby') redirect(302, `/adventures/${params.id}/lobby`);
          if (adv.status === 'active') redirect(302, `/adventures/${params.id}`);

          const [membership] = await db
              .select()
              .from(adventureMembers)
              .where(and(
                  eq(adventureMembers.adventureId, params.id),
                  eq(adventureMembers.userId, locals.user.id)
              ))
              .limit(1);

          if (!membership) error(403, 'You are not a member of this adventure');

          const members = await db
              .select({
                  userId: adventureMembers.userId,
                  role: adventureMembers.role,
                  username: users.username,
                  avatarUrl: users.avatarUrl
              })
              .from(adventureMembers)
              .innerJoin(users, eq(adventureMembers.userId, users.id))
              .where(eq(adventureMembers.adventureId, params.id));

          const [stateRow] = await db
              .select()
              .from(adventureState)
              .where(eq(adventureState.adventureId, params.id))
              .limit(1);

          let gameState = createInitialGameState(adv.worldSeed ?? '');
          if (stateRow) {
              try { gameState = migrateState(JSON.parse(stateRow.stateJson)); }
              catch { /* corrupted state â€” fall back to empty */ }
          }

          // Load ALL turns in chronological order (no limit â€” story is frozen)
          const turnRows = await db
              .select()
              .from(adventureTurns)
              .where(eq(adventureTurns.adventureId, params.id))
              .orderBy(asc(adventureTurns.turnNumber));

          const allTurns: TurnRecord[] = turnRows.map((r) => ({
              id: r.id,
              turnNumber: r.turnNumber,
              actorType: r.actorType as TurnRecord['actorType'],
              actorId: r.actorId,
              action: r.action,
              intent: r.intent as TurnRecord['intent'],
              status: (r.status ?? 'completed') as TurnRecord['status'],
              resolvedActionSummary: r.resolvedSummary ?? '',
              mechanicResults: JSON.parse(r.mechanicsJson) as TurnRecord['mechanicResults'],
              stateChanges: JSON.parse(r.stateChangesJson) as StateChange,
              narrativeText: r.narrativeText,
              timestamp: r.createdAt
          }));

          // Load ALL chat in chronological order (no limit)
          const chatRows = await db
              .select()
              .from(adventureChat)
              .where(eq(adventureChat.adventureId, params.id))
              .orderBy(asc(adventureChat.createdAt));

          const allChat = chatRows.map((r) => ({
              id: r.id,
              userId: r.userId,
              username: r.username,
              text: r.text,
              mentions: JSON.parse(r.mentionsJson) as string[],
              retroInvoked: r.retroInvoked,
              consumedByTurn: r.consumedByTurn,
              createdAt: r.createdAt
          }));

          // â”€â”€ Compute 14 stats â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
          const msPlayed = adv.updatedAt - adv.createdAt;
          const hoursPlayed = Math.floor(msPlayed / 3_600_000);
          const minutesPlayed = Math.floor((msPlayed % 3_600_000) / 60_000);

          const enemyRoles = new Set(['hostile', 'boss']);
          const enemiesDefeated = gameState.npcs.filter(n => !n.alive && enemyRoles.has(n.role)).length;
          const bossesDefeated  = gameState.npcs.filter(n => !n.alive && n.role === 'boss').length;
          const alliesLost      = gameState.npcs.filter(n => !n.alive && (n.role === 'ally' || n.role === 'companion')).length;

          const questsCompleted = gameState.quests.filter(q => q.status === 'completed').length;
          const questsFailed    = gameState.quests.filter(q => q.status === 'failed').length;
          const questsActive    = gameState.quests.filter(q => q.status === 'active' || q.status === 'available').length;

          const locationsVisited = gameState.locations.filter(l => l.visited).length;
          const locationsTotal   = gameState.locations.length;

          const totalXp   = gameState.characters.reduce((s, c) => s + (c.xp   ?? 0), 0);
          const totalGold = gameState.characters.reduce((s, c) => s + (c.gold ?? 0), 0);

          const itemsAcquired = allTurns.reduce((sum, t) => {
              const gained = (t.stateChanges as StateChange)?.itemsGained ?? [];
              return sum + gained.reduce((s, g) => s + (g.item?.quantity ?? 1), 0);
          }, 0);

          const stats = {
              hoursPlayed, minutesPlayed,
              totalTurns: allTurns.length,
              totalMessages: allChat.length,
              enemiesDefeated, bossesDefeated, alliesLost,
              questsCompleted, questsFailed, questsActive,
              locationsVisited, locationsTotal,
              totalXp, totalGold,
              daysElapsed: gameState.clock?.day ?? 1,
              itemsAcquired
          };

          return {
              adventure: adv,
              members,
              gameState,
              stats,
              allTurns,
              allChat,
              currentUserId: locals.user.id
          };
      };

CHANGE 8.3 â€” Create summary/+page.svelte
  File: routes/adventures/[id]/summary/+page.svelte  (NEW FILE)

  This file is the page component for the completed adventure chronicle.
  Important constraints:
    - NO PartySocket connection (story is frozen)
    - NO body/html overflow lock ($effect for scroll lock must NOT be added)
    - NO chat input, NO combat panel, NO dice roll UI
    - Normal scrollable page layout (no height constraints on root)
    - Uses GlassPanel component for party cards and quest/world panels
    - All CSS is scoped inside <style> using CSS custom properties from app.css

  â”€â”€ SECTION OVERVIEW â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

     - Each card shows:
       * Avatar circle with initials (first letter of each name word)
       * Avatar background: color-mix(in srgb, var(--accent) 20%, var(--surface))
       * Name (h3), race Â· class/level line, "Played by [username]" if member found
       * 4-stat grid: XP / HP (current/max) / AC / Gold
       * Death status (âš°ï¸ Fallen / ðŸ’¤ Stabilized) if applicable
       * <details> element for backstory (collapsed by default)
       * Inventory list: top 5 items + "+N moreâ€¦" overflow indicator

  4. Quest Chronicle ("Quest Chronicle" heading)
     - Three GlassPanel columns (auto-fill minmax 280px):
       * Completed quests â€” heading: "âœ“ Completed" in green (var(--accent-2))
       * Failed quests â€” heading: "âœ— Failed" in red (var(--danger))
       * Unresolved quests â€” heading: "â—Œ Unresolved" in muted colour
     - Each quest entry shows name, XP/gold rewards, and objectives
       with âœ“/â—‹ per objective (strikethrough on completed objectives)

  5. World & Encounters ("World & Encounters" heading)
     - Two-column grid (auto-fill minmax 300px):
       * Locations panel: list with coloured dot (accent = visited, border = unvisited)
         and type label
       * NPCs panel: table rows showing name / role / alive status
         NPCs sorted by role priority: boss â†’ hostile â†’ ally â†’ companion â†’
         quest-giver â†’ merchant â†’ neutral

  6. Full Transcript ("The Story" heading)
     - Wrapped in a single GlassPanel
     - buildTranscript() function merges allTurns + allChat:
       * Sort combined array by timestamp
       * From chat: kind='party', username=c.username
       * From GM turns: kind='gm-narration' (narrativeText field)
       * From turns with mechanic results: kind='mechanic' (formatted summary)
     - Collapsed by default: shows last 20 messages
     - "Show full story (N messages)" expand button
     - "Collapse story" button when expanded
     - Transcript capped at max-height: 600px with overflow-y: auto when collapsed
     - Message styles:
       * gm-narration: left border 3px var(--accent), italic text
       * mechanic:     left border 3px var(--accent-2), smaller muted text
       * system:       centred, muted
       * party:        plain, author name above in var(--accent) colour

================================================================================
  APPENDIX A â€” THEMEPICKER COMPONENT (no changes, reference only)
  Purpose: Documents the ThemePicker component so implementers understand
           the theme selection mechanism referenced by Nav.svelte.
  File: lib/components/ThemePicker.svelte (READ-ONLY reference)
================================================================================

  ThemePicker is already fully implemented in the original codebase.
  It was NOT modified in these sessions. It is documented here purely
  as a reference because it is imported in Nav.svelte.

  Key APIs it exposes (from lib/stores/themeStore.ts):
    - THEMES: ThemeMeta[] â€” full list of all 12 theme objects, split into
        group: 'original' | 'eccentric'; each has id, name, description,
        swatchBg, swatchAccent, swatchAccent2, colorScheme
    - themeStore: Svelte writable â€” current ThemeId as reactive store
    - setTheme(id: ThemeId): void â€” saves to localStorage + applies data-theme
    - ThemeId type: union of all 12 theme id strings

  The ThemePicker renders:
    - A trigger button (coloured dot + "Theme" label + chevron)
    - A popover with two sections:
        Originals: arcane-celestial, dark-academia, void-astral, silver-scroll,
                   forge-iron, morning-mist, midnight-court, clean-slate
        Eccentrics: blood-oath, vellum-quill, sakura-court, frozen-spire
    - Each swatch shows 3 colour dots (bg, accent, accent-2) + DARK/LIGHT badge
    - Active theme has a âœ“ checkmark and highlighted border
    - Escape key closes the popover; clicking outside the popover closes it
    - Client-only: no server state, no network calls; local storage only

  APPENDIX B â€” GLASSPANEL COMPONENT (no changes, reference only)
  Purpose: Documents the GlassPanel component so implementers understand
           the surface container used throughout the summary page and cards.
  File: lib/components/GlassPanel.svelte (READ-ONLY reference)
================================================================================

  GlassPanel is already fully implemented in the original codebase.
  It was NOT modified in these sessions. It is used as a container in:
    - summary/+page.svelte (party cards, quest panels, world panels, transcript)

  Props:
    - padding?: string â€” CSS padding value, applied as inline style (default varies)

  Rendered HTML:

      <div class="glass-panel" style="padding: {padding}">
          <slot />  (or Svelte 5 {#snippet children}, equivalent)
      </div>

  CSS (inside the component):

      .glass-panel {
          background: var(--surface);
          border: 1px solid var(--border);
          border-radius: var(--radius);
          box-shadow: var(--shadow);
          backdrop-filter: blur(var(--blur-glass));
          -webkit-backdrop-filter: blur(var(--blur-glass));
      }

  Note: The --shadow variable is set to 'none' inside .adventure-screen
  (see CHANGE 4.4) which removes the shadow from all GlassPanels within
  the active adventure page. The summary page does NOT do this, so
  GlassPanels on the summary page retain their default shadow.

  APPENDIX C â€” DATABASE SCHEMA (no changes, reference only)
  Purpose: Documents the SQLite tables used by the new and modified server
           files, so implementers can verify their schema matches.
  All tables are defined in lib/server/db/schema.ts
================================================================================

  adventures
    id            text PRIMARY KEY
    name          text NOT NULL
    ownerId       text NOT NULL  (FK â†’ users.id)
    worldSeed     text
    mode          text           ('solo' | 'multiplayer')
    status        text           ('lobby' | 'active' | 'completed')
    createdAt     integer        (Unix ms timestamp)
    updatedAt     integer        (Unix ms timestamp)

  adventureMembers
    adventureId   text  (FK â†’ adventures.id)
    userId        text  (FK â†’ users.id)
    role          text  ('owner' | 'player')
    PRIMARY KEY (adventureId, userId)

  adventureState
    adventureId   text  (FK â†’ adventures.id)
    stateJson     text  (JSON-serialised GameState)

  adventureTurns
    id            text PRIMARY KEY
    adventureId   text  (FK â†’ adventures.id)
    turnNumber    integer
    actorType     text
    actorId       text
    action        text
    intent        text  (JSON)
    status        text
    resolvedSummary text
    mechanicsJson text  (JSON array of MechanicResult)
    stateChangesJson text (JSON StateChange object)
    narrativeText text
    createdAt     integer

  adventureChat
    id            text PRIMARY KEY
    adventureId   text  (FK â†’ adventures.id)
    userId        text
    username      text
    text          text
    mentionsJson  text  (JSON string[])
    retroInvoked  integer (boolean)
    consumedByTurn text
    createdAt     integer

  users
    id            text PRIMARY KEY
    username      text NOT NULL
    avatarUrl     text

  GROUP 9 â€” DISPLAY HEADING DESCENDER CLIP FIX
  Purpose: Letters with descenders (g, y, p, q, Q, Y) were visually cut off
           on all large page-title headings. The bottom stroke of those glyphs
           appeared to be sliced by an invisible horizontal line.
  Root cause: Every affected heading uses  -webkit-background-clip: text
              (gradient fill). With this technique the browser paints the
              gradient only inside the element's own CSS box. Line-heights of
              1.1 â€“ 1.15 produce a box that is too tight: descenders extend
              below the line box, land outside the painted region, and become
              invisible because -webkit-text-fill-color: transparent has made
              the real text colour transparent.
  Fix: Add padding-bottom: 0.15em (0.1em for the summary page heading) to
       each affected element. Padding expands the element's box downward,
       giving the background-clip paint region enough room to cover every
       descender. Line-height was also nudged from 1.1/1.15 â†’ 1.2/1.15 to
       add consistent breathing room between wrapped lines.
       The summary page hero-title does NOT use background-clip (plain text
       colour) but received the same line-height and padding-bottom treatment
       to prevent any parent overflow: hidden from clipping descenders.
  Files modified: routes/+page.svelte
                  routes/about/+page.svelte
                  routes/reviews/+page.svelte
                  routes/adventures/[id]/summary/+page.svelte
  Session date: April 2, 2026
================================================================================

  File: routes/+page.svelte
  Class: .hero-title

  ORIGINAL:
      .hero-title {
          font-family: var(--font-display);
          font-size: clamp(2.5rem, 6vw, 4.5rem);
          font-weight: 800;
          line-height: 1.1;
          margin: 0 0 1.5rem;
          background: linear-gradient(135deg, var(--text) 0%, var(--accent) 100%);

          -webkit-text-fill-color: transparent;

          margin: 0 0 1.5rem;
          padding-bottom: 0.15em;
          background: linear-gradient(135deg, var(--text) 0%, var(--accent) 100%);

CHANGE 10.1 â€” Reorder RACES array
  File: site/src/lib/game/data/races.ts
  Location: export const RACES: RaceDefinition[] = [ ... ]

  Previous order: Human, Elf, Dwarf, Halfling, Half-Orc, Gnome, Tiefling,
                  Dragonborn, Half-Elf

  New order:      Human, Elf, Half-Elf, Half-Orc, Dragonborn, Tiefling,
                  Dwarf, Halfling, Gnome

  Only the array element order was changed. No race object contents were
  modified (descriptions, stat blocks, traits, subraces all unchanged).

CHANGE 10.2 â€” Reorder Dragonborn subraces for 2-column grid
  File: site/src/lib/game/data/races.ts
  Location: subraces array inside the 'dragonborn' race object

  Previous order: black, blue, brass, bronze, copper, gold, green, red,
                  silver, white (alphabetical)

  New order:      black, copper, blue, bronze, red, brass, gold, green,
                  white, silver

  Rationale: The 2-column Chromatic/Metallic grid (Phase 2e) will pair
  rows by damage type. The subrace array order drives the pairing:
    Row 1 â€” Black (Acid/Line)       | Copper (Acid/Line)
    Row 2 â€” Blue (Lightning/Line)   | Bronze (Lightning/Line)
    Row 3 â€” Red (Fire/Cone)         | Brass (Fire/Line)
    Row 4 â€” Gold (Fire/Cone)        | Green (Poison/Cone)  [no metallic pair for green]
    Row 5 â€” White (Cold/Cone)       | Silver (Cold/Cone)

  No subrace object content was modified.

CHANGE 10.3 â€” Remove 'unaligned' from Alignment type
  File: site/src/lib/game/types.ts
  Location: export type Alignment = ...

  ORIGINAL (last two lines of the union):
      | 'neutral-evil'
      | 'chaotic-evil'
      | 'unaligned';

  CHANGED TO:
      | 'neutral-evil'
      | 'chaotic-evil';

  The 'unaligned' value is not a valid player alignment â€” it applies only
  to monsters. Removing it from the type union enforces correctness at the
  TypeScript level.
  Note: The corresponding UI entry { value: 'unaligned', label: 'Unaligned' }
  in CharacterCreation.svelte line 88 will be removed in Phase 2f, completing
  the cleanup.

CHANGE 11.1 â€” Race list sidebar: remove JS truncation
  File: lib/components/CharacterCreation.svelte
  Location: {#each RACES as race} loop, the option-sub span (~line 818)

  ORIGINAL (NOTE: the 'Ã¢â‚¬Â¦' below is the literal corrupted string you will
  find in the source file â€” it is NOT a document encoding error):
      <span class="option-sub">{race.description.length > 70 ? race.description.slice(0, 70) + 'Ã¢â‚¬Â¦' : race.description}</span>

  CHANGED TO:
      <span class="option-sub">{race.description}</span>

  Explanation:
    The JS truncation was producing garbled output due to encoding corruption
    of the ellipsis character. The .option-sub CSS selector already had
    -webkit-line-clamp: 2 and overflow: hidden applied, so CSS clipping alone
    is sufficient. Removing the JS slice also eliminates the corrupted
    character entirely.

CHANGE 11.2 â€” Race stat tag row: prefix Size and combine Languages
  File: lib/components/CharacterCreation.svelte
  Location: <div class="tag-row"> inside the race detail pane

  ORIGINAL:
      <span class="tag">{raceDef.size}</span>
      {#each raceDef.languages as lang}
          <span class="tag">{lang}</span>
      {/each}

  CHANGED TO:
      <span class="tag">Size: {raceDef.size}</span>
      <span class="tag">Languages: {[...raceDef.languages, ...(subraceDef?.extraLanguages ?? [])].join(', ')}</span>

  Explanation:
    The Size tag lacked its label. Languages were shown as individual tags
    with no label. The new single Languages tag joins the base race languages
    with any subrace extraLanguages (e.g. Drow adds Undercommon), so the tag
    always reflects the complete language set for the current race+subrace
    combination.

CHANGE 11.3 â€” Reorder detail pane: Subrace picker above Ability Bonuses + Traits
  File: lib/components/CharacterCreation.svelte
  Location: Right-hand detail pane inside Step 0 (Race)

  ORIGINAL ORDER:
      description â†’ tag-row â†’ Ability Bonuses â†’ Racial Traits â†’ Subraces

  NEW ORDER:
      description â†’ tag-row â†’ Subrace picker â†’ Ability Bonuses â†’ Racial Traits

  Implementation: Moved the entire <!-- Subraces --> {#if} block (the
  detail-section containing the subrace card-list / Dragonborn grid) from
  after "Traits" to immediately after the tag-row div, before the
  "Ability Bonuses" detail-section.

  Rationale: Subrace selection changes the ability bonuses displayed, so
  the user should pick a subrace before seeing the bonuses and traits that

  GROUP 12 â€” CHARACTER CREATION SVELTE TEMPLATE FIXES (Phase 2 â€” Part 2)

CHANGE 12.1 â€” Effective darkvision: subrace override $derived
  File: lib/components/CharacterCreation.svelte
  Location: Script block, immediately after the subraceDef $derived

  ADD after:
      let subraceDef = $derived(form.subrace ? getSubrace(form.race, form.subrace) : undefined);

  NEW LINE:
      let effectiveDarkvision = $derived(
          (subraceDef?.traits.flatMap(t => t.effects).find(e => e.tag === 'darkvision') as { tag: 'darkvision'; range: number } | undefined)?.range
          ?? raceDef?.darkvision
          ?? 0
      );

  Also change the tag-row darkvision span from:
      {#if raceDef.darkvision > 0}
          <span class="tag">Darkvision {raceDef.darkvision} ft.</span>
      {/if}

  To:
      {#if effectiveDarkvision > 0}
          <span class="tag">Darkvision {effectiveDarkvision} ft.</span>
      {/if}

  Explanation:
    Some subraces override the base race darkvision range via a
    { tag: 'darkvision', range: N } effect on a subrace trait. The Dark Elf
    (Drow) subrace sets range: 120, overriding the base Elf's 60 ft. The
    derived walks subrace traits, finds the first darkvision effect, and
    falls back to raceDef.darkvision if absent.

  replaced with a purpose-built 2-column CSS grid. All other races retain
  the original card-list.

  Grid pairs (left = Chromatic, right = Metallic):
      Black / Copper   (Acid â€” Line)
      Blue  / Bronze   (Lightning â€” Line)
      Red   / Brass    (Fire â€” Cone / Line)
      empty / Gold     (Fire â€” Cone)
      Green / empty    (Poison â€” Cone)
      White / Silver   (Cold â€” Cone)

  Card subtitle is extracted at render time:
      sr.traits[0]?.name + ' â€” ' + capitalize(breathWeaponShape)
  where breathWeaponShape comes from the 'breath-weapon' effect on the
  subrace's first trait (shape: 'line' | 'cone').

  New CSS selectors added to <style>:
      .subrace-dragon-grid  â€” display: grid; grid-template-columns: 1fr 1fr; gap: 0.35rem
      .dragon-col-header    â€” uppercase label row ("Chromatic" / "Metallic")
      .dragon-empty         â€” invisible placeholder to hold grid alignment

  Relies on Dragonborn subraces being ordered correctly (CHANGE 10.2).

================================================================================
  GROUP 13 â€” CHARACTER CREATION ENCODING FIXES & POINT BUY (Phase 2gâ€“2i)
  Purpose: Fix all UTF-8 double-encoding corruption, remove feat description
           truncation, add point buy clamping and improved hints.
  Files modified: site/src/lib/components/CharacterCreation.svelte
  Session date: April 2, 2026

  Root cause of encoding corruption:
    The file's original author likely edited the file in an editor that
    re-saved it treating the UTF-8 content as Latin-1/Windows-1252, causing
    each 2â€“3 byte UTF-8 sequence to be interpreted as individual Latin-1
    characters and then re-encoded as UTF-8. Result: every special character
    became a 2â€“4 character garbled sequence. The fix was applied via byte-
    level PowerShell replacement targeting the known corrupt byte patterns.
================================================================================

CHANGE 13.1 â€” Global encoding corruption fix (2g)
  File: lib/components/CharacterCreation.svelte
  Method: PowerShell [System.IO.File]::ReadAllText + string Replace + WriteAllText

  Five corruption patterns replaced globally across the file (18 total instances):

  Pattern   | Corrupt chars (codepoints)      | Correct char (codepoint)
  ----------|----------------------------------|---------------------------
  Em dash   | [226, 8364, 8221] â†’ Ã¢ + â‚¬ + "  | â€” (8212, U+2014)
  Bullet    | [226, 8364, 162]  â†’ Ã¢ + â‚¬ + Â¢  | â€¢ (8226, U+2022)
  Math minus| [226, 710, 8217]  â†’ Ã¢ + Ë† + '  | - (45, ASCII hyphen-minus)
  Middle dot| [194, 183]        â†’ Ã‚ + Â·       | Â· (183, U+00B7)
  Ellipsis  | [226, 8364, 166]  â†’ Ã¢ + â‚¬ + Â¦  | â€¦ (8230, U+2026)

  Instance counts fixed:
    Em dash   â€” 4 instances (formatLabel return, summary hint, 2Ã— summary-details)
    Bullet    â€” 1 instance (err-item span in error strip)
    Math minus â€” 1 instance (ab-btn minus button label in ability builder)
    Middle dot â€” 9 instances (step comment separators + 2 in summary hint line)
    Ellipsis  â€” 3 instances (Creatingâ€¦ button, feat truncation expression, one other)

  Specific locations called out in plan (2g table):
    ~~Line 819: removed by 2a (already done)~~
    Line ~797: err-item bullet â†’ fixed (now â€¢)
    Line ~942: ellipsis in feat truncation â†’ fixed, then removed (see CHANGE 13.2)
    Line ~1184: minus button content â†’ fixed (now -)
    Line ~1201: em dash in locked-in hint â†’ fixed (now â€”)  [also covers 2i]
    Line ~268: formatLabel return â†’ fixed (now 'â€”')
    Line ~1427: middle dot separators â†’ fixed (now Â·)
    Line ~1452: summary hint separators + em dash fallback â†’ fixed
    Line ~1487: 'Creatingâ€¦' button â†’ fixed (now 'Creatingâ€¦')

CHANGE 13.2 â€” Remove feat description truncation (2g line 917)
  File: lib/components/CharacterCreation.svelte

CHANGE 13.3 â€” Point buy: updateAbility() value clamping (2h)
  File: lib/components/CharacterCreation.svelte
  Location: function updateAbility(), script block

  ORIGINAL:
      function updateAbility(ability: AbilityName, value: string) {
          const next = Number(value);
          if (!form.abilityAssignment || Number.isNaN(next)) return;
          form.abilityAssignment = { ...form.abilityAssignment, [ability]: next };
          syncSpellState();
      }

  CHANGED TO:
      function updateAbility(ability: AbilityName, value: string) {
          const next = Number(value);
          if (!form.abilityAssignment || Number.isNaN(next)) return;
          const min = form.statMethod === 'rolled' ? 3 : 8;
          const max = form.statMethod === 'rolled' ? 18 : 15;
          form.abilityAssignment = { ...form.abilityAssignment, [ability]: Math.min(max, Math.max(min, next)) };
          syncSpellState();
      }

  Explanation: HTML min/max attributes only block the spinner buttons;
  typed values bypass them. Clamping in JS ensures no value outside the
  legal range can persist in state regardless of input method.
  Range: point-buy â†’ 8â€“15, rolled â†’ 3â€“18, standard â†’ (no input, N/A).

CHANGE 13.4 â€” Point buy: budget bar hint line + correct block structure (2h)
  File: lib/components/CharacterCreation.svelte
  Location: Abilities step (step === 3), the point-buy conditional block and
            the ability-grid-builder loop that follows it.

  IMPORTANT: The {#if form.statMethod === 'point-buy'} block must be CLOSED
  before the <div class="ability-grid-builder"> wrapper. The hint <p> belongs
  INSIDE the {#if} block (visible only in point-buy mode), with {/if} following
  it. The {#each abilityOrder as ability} loop is INSIDE the grid div, NOT
  inside the {#if} block â€” abilities are always rendered regardless of method.

  CORRECT BLOCK STRUCTURE (replace the existing point-buy block + grid div):

      {#if form.statMethod === 'point-buy'}
          <div class="budget-bar" class:over={!pointBuySummary.valid && pointBuySummary.remaining < 0}>
              <span>Points spent: <strong>{pointBuySummary.spent}</strong> / 27</span>
              <span>Remaining: <strong>{pointBuySummary.remaining}</strong></span>
          </div>
          <p class="hint">Each score: 8 (0 pts) to 15 (9 pts) â€” total budget: 27 pts</p>
      {/if}

      <div class="ability-grid-builder">
          {#each abilityOrder as ability}
              {@const base = form.abilityAssignment?.[ability] ?? 10}
              ... (ability card content â€” unchanged)
          {/each}
      </div>

  Key rules enforced by this structure:
    1. The budget-bar and hint are only shown in point-buy mode.
    2. The {/if} closes BEFORE the grid div â€” never nest {#each} inside {#if}.
    3. The ability cards render in all three stat methods (standard, rolled, point-buy).
  
  CSS note: .hint uses the existing muted small-text style (no new CSS needed).

  GROUP 14 â€” HOTFIX: TEMPLATE STRUCTURE REGRESSION (Session 4)
  Purpose: Restore the correct Svelte block structure in CharacterCreation.svelte
           that was accidentally destroyed during the CHANGE 13.4 edit.
  Files modified: site/src/lib/components/CharacterCreation.svelte
  Session date: April 6, 2026

  Root cause:
    The replace_string_in_file edit for CHANGE 13.4 used an oldString that
    extended into the surrounding structural lines ({/if}, <div>, {#each}) but
    the newString omitted those lines. As a result three structural lines were
    silently deleted:
      (1) {/if}  â€” closing the point-buy conditional
      (2) <div class="ability-grid-builder">  â€” wrapper for the ability cards
      (3) {#each abilityOrder as ability}  â€” loop opener
    This left a dangling {/each} with no matching {#each}, causing Svelte to
    throw "Expected token if" at compile time. Every route importing the
    component returned HTTP 500.

  CHANGE 13.4 has been updated in this document to specify the full correct
  block structure (see above) so it cannot be reproduced incorrectly.

CHANGE 15.1 â€” Per-method independent ability state (Phase A)
  File: lib/components/CharacterCreation.svelte
  Location: Script block â€” new $state vars after rolledSeed, rewritten
            setStatMethod, updated rerollStats.

  PROBLEM: form.abilityAssignment was a single reactive object shared across
  all three stat methods. Switching methods reset or overwrote the other
  method's values, so e.g. a point-buy score of 1599 would appear in standard
  array when switching.

  SOLUTION: Three save-slots.

  NEW STATE (add after let rolledSeed = $state(0)):
      let savedStandard = $state<AbilityScores>({ str: 15, dex: 13, con: 14, int: 10, wis: 12, cha: 8 });
      let savedPointBuy = $state<AbilityScores>({ str: 8, dex: 8, con: 8, int: 8, wis: 8, cha: 8 });
      let savedRolled   = $state<AbilityScores>({ str: 10, dex: 10, con: 10, int: 10, wis: 10, cha: 10 });

  REWRITE setStatMethod to save then restore:
      function setStatMethod(method) {
          // 1. Save departing method's current assignment
          if (form.abilityAssignment) {
              if (form.statMethod === 'standard')  savedStandard = { ...form.abilityAssignment };
              else if (form.statMethod === 'point-buy') savedPointBuy = { ...form.abilityAssignment };
              else if (form.statMethod === 'rolled')    savedRolled  = { ...form.abilityAssignment };
          }
          // 2. Switch and restore
          form.statMethod = method;
          if (method === 'standard')  { form.abilityAssignment = { ...savedStandard };  syncStandardSlots(); syncSpellState(); }
          if (method === 'point-buy') { form.abilityAssignment = { ...savedPointBuy };  syncSpellState(); }
          if (method === 'rolled') {
              if (rolledSeed === 0) rerollStats(); // first visit â€” generate fresh roll
              else { form.abilityAssignment = { ...savedRolled }; syncSpellState(); }
          }
      }

  ADD to rerollStats: after building assignment, before syncSpellState():
      savedRolled = { ...assignment };

  Rule: NEVER call rerollStats() when switching back to 'rolled' if rolledSeed > 0.
  This preserves the player's current roll set across method switches.

CHANGE 15.2 â€” Rolled mode: dice tracking + enlarged 3Ã—2 grid (Phase B)
  File: lib/components/CharacterCreation.svelte

  NEW STATE (after savedRolled):
      let rolledDice = $state<Record<AbilityName, number[]>>({
          str: [], dex: [], con: [], int: [], wis: [], cha: []
      });

  REWRITE roll4d6DropLowest â€” returns object with dice array:
      function roll4d6DropLowest(): { total: number; dice: number[] } {
          const dice = Array.from({ length: 4 }, () =>
              Math.floor(Math.random() * 6) + 1).sort((a, b) => a - b);
          return { total: dice[1] + dice[2] + dice[3], dice };
      }
      // dice[0] = dropped (lowest), dice[1..3] = kept (ascending)

  REWRITE rerollStats body â€” sort by .total, populate rolledDice:
      const rollResults = Array.from({ length: 6 }, () =>
          roll4d6DropLowest()).sort((a, b) => b.total - a.total);
      const dmap: Record<AbilityName, number[]> = { str:[],dex:[],con:[],int:[],wis:[],cha:[] };
      ordered.forEach((ability, index) => {
          assignment[ability] = rollResults[index].total;
          dmap[ability] = rollResults[index].dice;
      });
      rolledDice = dmap;

  TEMPLATE â€” ability-grid-builder:
      <div class="ability-grid-builder" class:rolled={form.statMethod === 'rolled'}>

  TEMPLATE â€” ability card becomes row layout when rolled:
      <div class="ability-builder-card" class:rolled-card={form.statMethod === 'rolled'}>
          <div class="ab-left">
              ... (label, controls [point-buy only], breakdown, total)
          </div>
          {#if form.statMethod === 'rolled' && rolledDice[ability].length > 0}
              {@const d = rolledDice[ability]}
              <div class="dice-display">
                  <span class="dice-rolled">{d[3]} Â· {d[2]} Â· {d[1]} Â· <s>{d[0]}</s></span>
                  <span class="dice-calc">kept: {d[1]}+{d[2]}+{d[3]} = {d[1]+d[2]+d[3]}</span>
              </div>
          {/if}
      </div>
      <!-- dice[0] displayed as <s> (struck-through); d[3] highest value shown first -->

  NEW CSS:
      .ability-grid-builder.rolled { grid-template-columns: repeat(3, 1fr); }
      .ability-builder-card.rolled-card { flex-direction: row; justify-content: space-between;
          align-items: center; padding: 0.85rem 0.9rem; min-height: 5rem; gap: 0.5rem; }
      .ab-left { display: flex; flex-direction: column; align-items: center; gap: 0.3rem; }
      .dice-display { display: flex; flex-direction: column; align-items: flex-end;
          gap: 0.3rem; flex: 1; }
      .dice-rolled { font-size: 0.8rem; color: var(--text-muted); font-family: monospace; }
      .dice-rolled s { color: rgba(255,96,96,0.65); text-decoration-color: rgba(255,96,96,0.65); }
      .dice-calc { font-size: 0.78rem; color: var(--accent); }

CHANGE 15.3 â€” Standard array: drag-and-drop assignment (Phase C)
  File: lib/components/CharacterCreation.svelte

  NEW STATE (after rolledDice â€” type alias + three state vars):
      type StandardDragSrc =
          | { value: number; from: 'pool' }
          | { value: number; from: 'slot'; ability: AbilityName };
      let standardSlots  = $state<Partial<Record<AbilityName, number>>>
          ({ str: 15, dex: 13, con: 14, int: 10, wis: 12, cha: 8 });
      let dragSource     = $state<StandardDragSrc | null>(null);
      let dragOverTarget = $state<AbilityName | 'pool' | null>(null);

  NEW DERIVED (after pointBuySummary):
      let standardPool = $derived.by(() => {
          const used = new Set(Object.values(standardSlots)
              .filter((v): v is number => v !== undefined));
          return STANDARD_ARRAY.filter(v => !used.has(v));
      });

  NEW FUNCTIONS (between setStatMethod and updateAbility):

      syncStandardSlots()       â€” copies savedStandard â†’ standardSlots
                                  called when entering standard mode
      syncStandardAssignment()  â€” writes standardSlots â†’ form.abilityAssignment,
                                  saves back to savedStandard, calls syncSpellState
      startDrag(src)            â€” sets dragSource = src
      endDrag()                 â€” clears dragSource and dragOverTarget
      dropOnSlot(target)        â€” moves/swaps chip from pool or another slot into target
      dropOnPool()              â€” unassigns chip from a slot, returns to pool

  DRAG RULES:
      pool chip â†’ ability slot : assigns value to slot
      slot chip â†’ another slot : swaps the two values
      slot chip â†’ pool         : unassigns, value returns to pool tray
      A local 'src = dragSource' copy is used inside handlers to allow TypeScript
      to narrow the discriminated union (from 'pool' | 'slot').

  TEMPLATE â€” inside ability card ab-left, after point-buy controls:
      {:else if form.statMethod === 'standard'}
          <div class="ab-drop-slot"
               class:occupied={standardSlots[ability] !== undefined}
               class:drag-over={dragOverTarget === ability}
               ondragover ...  ondragleave ...  ondrop={() => dropOnSlot(ability)}>
              {#if standardSlots[ability] !== undefined}
                  <div class="pool-chip in-slot" draggable="true"
                       ondragstart={() => startDrag({ value: standardSlots[ability]!,
                           from: 'slot', ability })}>
                      {standardSlots[ability]}
                  </div>
              {:else}
                  <span class="drop-hint">drop here</span>
              {/if}
          </div>

  TEMPLATE â€” pool tray below ability grid (replaces old standard hint <p>):
      {#if form.statMethod === 'standard'}
          <div class="standard-pool" class:drag-over-pool ondragover ondrop={() => dropOnPool()}>
              {#each standardPool as val (val)}
                  <div class="pool-chip" draggable="true"
                       ondragstart={() => startDrag({ value: val, from: 'pool' })}>
                      {val}
                  </div>
              {/each}
              {#if standardPool.length === 0}
                  <span class="pool-empty">All values assigned</span>
              {/if}
          </div>
          <p class="standard-hint">Assign the values {STANDARD_ARRAY.join(', ')} to your abilities in any order.</p>
      {/if}

  VALIDATION UPDATE (getStepErrors step 3):
      ORIGINAL: no check for incomplete standard array
      ADDED:
          } else if (form.statMethod === 'standard' && standardPool.length > 0) {
              issues.push({ field: 'abilityAssignment',
                  message: `Assign all 6 values. Unplaced: ${standardPool.join(', ')}.` });

  NEW CSS: .standard-pool, .standard-pool.drag-over-pool, .pool-chip,
           .pool-chip:active, .pool-chip.in-slot, .pool-empty, .ab-drop-slot,
           .ab-drop-slot.drag-over, .drop-hint, .standard-hint (font-size: 1rem)

  GROUP 16 â€” HOTFIX: validateStep BRACE REGRESSION (Session 5)
  Purpose: Restore correct brace structure in validateStep() step===3 block.
  Files modified: site/src/lib/components/CharacterCreation.svelte
  Session date: April 6, 2026

  Root cause:
    The multi_replace_string_in_file call that added the standard-pool validation
    branch to validateStep() produced malformed output. The inserted } else if
    line had 4-tab indentation instead of 3-tab, which caused the outer
    if (step === 3) closing brace } to land BEFORE the else-if body was closed.
    The entire rest of validateStep (step 4, step 5, and all subsequent functions)
    became syntactically nested inside an unclosed else-if block, leaving braces
    unbalanced at the </script> tag â†’ "Unexpected token" parse error line 814.

  Pattern to avoid: When a multi_replace newString contains template literals
    (backtick strings with ${...}) nested inside JSON string parameters, the
    indentation of closing braces must be verified against 0-indexed line
    numbers with a PowerShell preview before writing. Always check the closing
    } count after any edit that changes brace nesting.

CHANGE 17.3 â€” Fix departure save in setStatMethod
  File: lib/components/CharacterCreation.svelte
  Location: setStatMethod(), departure guard (~line 450)

  OLD: if (form.statMethod === 'standard') savedStandard = { ...form.abilityAssignment };
  NEW: if (form.statMethod === 'standard') savedStandard = { ...standardSlots };

  Reason: Saving form.abilityAssignment (a full 6-key object with base-fallback
  10s) would inflate standardSlots on the return visit with phantom "10" chips
  appearing pre-placed. Saving standardSlots (the sparse partial) correctly
  preserves only the chips the user actually dragged onto slots.

CHANGE 17.4 â€” Fix standard-arrival block in setStatMethod
  File: lib/components/CharacterCreation.svelte
  Location: setStatMethod(), if (method === 'standard') block (~lines 455-458)

  OLD:
      if (method === 'standard') {
          form.abilityAssignment = { ...savedStandard };
          syncStandardSlots();
          syncSpellState();
      }
  NEW:
      if (method === 'standard') {
          syncStandardSlots();
          syncStandardAssignment();
      }

  Reason: Direct spread of savedStandard (now a Partial) into form.abilityAssignment
  would produce an incomplete AbilityScores object. Calling syncStandardAssignment()
  instead correctly merges standardSlots over a base-10 fallback. syncSpellState()
  is now redundant here since syncStandardAssignment() calls it internally.

================================================================================
CHANGE 17.5 â€” Remove savedStandard sync from syncStandardAssignment
  File: lib/components/CharacterCreation.svelte
  Location: syncStandardAssignment() body (~line 480)

  Removed line: savedStandard = { ...form.abilityAssignment };

  Reason: syncStandardAssignment() is called on every drag-drop event. Syncing
  savedStandard from form.abilityAssignment (full 6 keys + base fallbacks) on
  every drop would immediately corrupt savedStandard with phantom fallback values,
  undoing the empty-pool fix. savedStandard is now only written in the departure
  save of setStatMethod.

================================================================================
  GROUP 19 â€” ORANGE & LEAD DRAGONBORN + GRID REORDER + TYPE SEPARATORS (Session 6)
  Purpose: Add two new Dragonborn subraces (Orange/Fire and Lead/Poison),
           reorder the entire 2-column subrace grid so fire is at the top and
           poison at the bottom, align damage types across columns, order
           chromatics by colour spectrum and metallics by precious-metal value,
           and add thin CSS divider lines between each damage-type group.
  Files modified: site/src/lib/game/data/races.ts
                  site/src/lib/components/CharacterCreation.svelte
  Session date: April 6, 2026

  New subrace design decisions:
    Orange (Chromatic/Fire) â€” copyright-clear; no TTRPG publisher has ever
      claimed "Orange Dragon" as a type. Orange is biology's universal warning
      colour (dart frogs, monarch butterflies) but shares fire damage with Red
      for a second chromatic fire entry at the top of the grid. Mechanics are
      identical to Red (15 ft. cone, fire damage + fire resistance).
    Lead (Metallic/Poison) â€” copyright-clear; no D&D edition, supplement, or
      third-party publisher has published a "Lead Dragon" type. Lead's real-
      world toxicology (accumulative heavy-metal poisoning, cognitive effects,
      "sugar of lead" sweet scent masking danger) makes it narratively distinct
      from Green. Mechanics are identical to Green (15 ft. cone, poison damage
      + poison resistance).

  New grid order:
    Row 1 â€” Red (Fire/Cone)     | Gold (Fire/Cone)
    Row 2 â€” Orange (Fire/Cone)  | Brass (Fire/Line)
    â”€â”€ fire separator â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
    Row 3 â€” Blue (Lightning/Line) | Bronze (Lightning/Line)
    â”€â”€ lightning separator â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
    Row 4 â€” White (Cold/Cone)   | Silver (Cold/Cone)
    â”€â”€ cold separator â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
    Row 5 â€” Black (Acid/Line)   | Copper (Acid/Line)
    â”€â”€ acid separator â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
    Row 6 â€” Green (Poison/Cone) | Lead (Poison/Cone)

  Ordering rationale:
    Chromatic column â€” spectrum order (Red â†’ Orange â†’ Blue â†’ White â†’ Black â†’
      Green). Yellow is skipped (no yellow subrace). White and Black are
      achromatic so fall after the spectral colours before the non-colour Green.
    Metallic column â€” precious-metal value order (Gold â†’ Brass â†’ Bronze â†’
      Silver â†’ Copper â†’ Lead). Lead is least valuable and most toxic, naturally
      anchoring the poison row.
    Cross-column type matching is the primary constraint â€” both entries in a
      row share the same damage type. The spectrum/value ordering is applied
      as a secondary constraint within that requirement.

GROUP 20 â€” COMBAT MECHANICS BUG FIXES (Issue 2: empty-creatures encounter guard)

  PURPOSE:
    A Testing.JSON session replay revealed that in two wolf encounters, the
    engine created an activeEncounter with zero combatants. Root cause: the
    engine's travel encounter template sets encounterStarted: { creatures: [] }
    as a signal for the AI to populate creatures, but (a) the merge strategy
    always preferred the engine's value over the AI's populated version, and
    (b) nothing stripped the empty-array form before createEncounter() was
    called. This produced a combatant-less encounter that cascaded into
    empty mechanics[], missing enemy HP, and low-confidence "i attack!" flags.

  CHANGES â€” all in lib/server/ai/adventure-turn.ts


CHANGE 20.1 â€” Explicit warning when sanitizeStateChanges strips empty creatures
  File: lib/server/ai/adventure-turn.ts
  Location: sanitizeStateChanges() â€” encounterStarted block, after the creature
            validation filter, before the content-evidence branches (~line 1947)

  ADDED (between the sc.encounterEnded conflict-check and the hasCombatEvidence
         regex, after validCreatures is computed):

      // Guard: empty creatures array is never valid â€” an encounter with no combatants
      // breaks the entire encounter system downstream.
      if (validCreatures.length === 0) {
          console.warn('[sanitize] encounterStarted.creatures is empty (0 valid entries) â€” stripped');
          // fall through: neither branch below sets clean.encounterStarted
      }

  The two existing branches (hasCombatEvidence and the no-narrative fallback)
  only fire when validCreatures.length > 0, so behaviour is unchanged; this
  adds an explicit log entry when the empty case is hit.


CHANGE 20.2 â€” mergeStateChanges: use GM creatures when engine template is empty
  File: lib/server/ai/adventure-turn.ts
  Location: mergeStateChanges() â€” encounterStarted line (~line 1172)

  ORIGINAL:
      // Encounter lifecycle
      encounterStarted: engine.encounterStarted ?? gm.encounterStarted,

  REPLACED WITH:
      // Encounter lifecycle
      // If the engine set an empty-template encounter (travel trigger), let the GM's
      // populated creatures fill it. Without this, AI-supplied creatures are discarded.
      encounterStarted: (() => {
          const eng = engine.encounterStarted;
          const gm_ = gm.encounterStarted;
          if (eng && !eng.creatures?.length && gm_?.creatures?.length) return gm_;
          return eng ?? gm_;
      })(),

  REASON: turn-executor.ts sets encounterStarted: { creatures: [] } as a travel
  encounter template. Before this fix, the engine's empty object was truthy so
  ?? never fell through to the AI's populated version, permanently discarding
  any creatures the AI correctly returned.


CHANGE 20.3 â€” Post-merge guard: strip any still-empty encounterStarted
  File: lib/server/ai/adventure-turn.ts
  Location: executeAdventureTurn() â€” full-gm-2pass path, immediately after the
            encounter classifier try/catch block (~line 751)

  ADDED:
      // Guard: strip any still-empty encounterStarted that survived the merge.
      // This catches engine travel templates that the AI failed to populate.
      if (finalStateChanges.encounterStarted && !finalStateChanges.encounterStarted.creatures?.length) {
          console.warn('[encounterMerge] encounterStarted.creatures is empty after merge â€” stripped (AI did not populate travel template)');
          delete finalStateChanges.encounterStarted;
      }

  This is the primary defence against the empty-creatures encounter reaching
  applyGMStateChanges.


CHANGE 20.4 â€” applyGMStateChanges: defensive guard before createEncounter()
  File: lib/server/ai/adventure-turn.ts
  Location: applyGMStateChanges() â€” encounterStarted block, immediately before
            the createEncounter() call (~line 2876)

  ORIGINAL:
      // Use the combat engine to roll initiative and build the encounter
      const allCombatCreatures = [...hostileNpcs, ...companionNpcs];
      const { encounter } = createEncounter(state, allCombatCreatures);
      initEncounterTurnOrder(state, encounter, state.npcs);
      state.activeEncounter = encounter;

  REPLACED WITH:
      // Use the combat engine to roll initiative and build the encounter.
      // Guard: skip creation if there are no combatants â€” an empty encounter
      // would leave state.activeEncounter set with no enemies to fight.
      const allCombatCreatures = [...hostileNpcs, ...companionNpcs];
      if (allCombatCreatures.length === 0) {
          console.warn('[applyGMStateChanges] encounterStarted produced no valid combatants â€” encounter creation skipped');
      } else {
          const { encounter } = createEncounter(state, allCombatCreatures);
          initEncounterTurnOrder(state, encounter, state.npcs);
          state.activeEncounter = encounter;
      }

  Belt-and-suspenders: even if an empty encounterStarted somehow reaches this
  function, no combatant-less activeEncounter is ever written to state.

  Verification: npx tsc --noEmit â€” 0 new errors introduced.

                unchanged; 184 passing tests unchanged; no regressions.

      parts.push(`- Create encounters or combat without using encounterStarted in stateChanges`);

  The inline parenthetical makes the two failure modes explicit: omitting the
