GROUP 22 â€” COMBAT MECHANICS BUG FIXES (Issue 9: auto-close encounter when all enemies defeated)

  PURPOSE:
    In full-gm-2pass mode the AI sometimes narrates a battle victory but
    forgets to include encounterEnded in the Pass 2 JSON. Without an explicit
    encounterEnded, state.activeEncounter is never cleared, the combat UI stays
    open, and XP is never awarded. This group adds an engine-side safety net
    that detects the "all combatants defeated but encounter still active" state
    and closes the encounter automatically, mirroring the existing
    applyGMStateChanges victory handler exactly.

  CHANGES â€” all in lib/server/ai/adventure-turn.ts


CHANGE 22.1 â€” Add allDefeated to combat import
  File: lib/server/ai/adventure-turn.ts
  Location: import line ~L32

  ORIGINAL:
      import { createEncounter, resolveEncounter, initEncounterTurnOrder, syncCombatantsFromState } from '$lib/game/combat';

  REPLACED WITH:
      import { createEncounter, resolveEncounter, allDefeated, initEncounterTurnOrder, syncCombatantsFromState } from '$lib/game/combat';

  allDefeated() was already exported from combat.ts but not imported in
  adventure-turn.ts. It checks whether every non-companion NPC combatant has
  defeated === true, which is the precise trigger condition for auto-close.


CHANGE 22.2 â€” Auto-close block in persistResolvedTurnAndState
  File: lib/server/ai/adventure-turn.ts
  Location: persistResolvedTurnAndState(), immediately after the
            syncCombatantsFromState(state, state.activeEncounter) call

  INSERTED BLOCK (runs after syncCombatantsFromState, before the periodic
  world-reaction check):

      // Auto-close encounter if all enemies are defeated but the GM forgot to emit encounterEnded.
      // Handles full-gm-2pass turns where the AI narrated a victory without including encounterEnded
      // in the state-extraction JSON. Must run AFTER syncCombatantsFromState (so defeated flags are fresh)
      // and AFTER applyGMStateChanges (so a GM-supplied encounterEnded is not double-processed).
      if (state.activeEncounter && !resolvedTurn.stateChanges.encounterEnded) {
          if (allDefeated(state, state.activeEncounter, 'npc')) {
              console.log('[autoClose] All enemies defeated â€” auto-closing encounter as victory');

              // Mirror the victory path in applyGMStateChanges: mark all non-companion enemy NPCs
              // as dead and record each change so the turn log has an accurate audit trail.
              for (const combatant of state.activeEncounter.combatants) {
                  if (combatant.type === 'npc') {
                      const npc = state.npcs.find((n) => n.id === combatant.referenceId);
                      if (npc && npc.role !== 'companion') {
                          combatant.defeated = true;
                          if (npc.alive !== false) {
                              npc.alive = false;
                              if (npc.statBlock) npc.statBlock.hp = 0;
                              if (!resolvedTurn.stateChanges.npcChanges) resolvedTurn.stateChanges.npcChanges = [];
                              resolvedTurn.stateChanges.npcChanges.push({ npcId: npc.id, field: 'alive', oldValue: true, newValue: false });
                          }
                      }
                  }
              }

              // Compute XP awards via the encounter resolver
              const encounterNpcIds = state.activeEncounter.combatants
                  .filter((c) => c.type === 'npc')
                  .map((c) => c.referenceId);
              const encounterNpcs = state.npcs.filter((n) => encounterNpcIds.includes(n.id));
              const partySize = state.characters.length;
              const resolution = resolveEncounter(state, state.activeEncounter, 'victory', encounterNpcs, partySize);

              // Apply XP to characters and surface awards in the turn record
              if (resolution.stateChange.xpAwarded) {
                  for (const award of resolution.stateChange.xpAwarded) {
                      const char = state.characters.find((c) => c.id === award.characterId);
                      if (char) char.xp += award.amount;
                  }
                  if (!resolvedTurn.stateChanges.xpAwarded) resolvedTurn.stateChanges.xpAwarded = [];
                  resolvedTurn.stateChanges.xpAwarded.push(...resolution.stateChange.xpAwarded);
              }

              // Emit encounterEnded so it appears in the persisted turn record
              resolvedTurn.stateChanges.encounterEnded = { outcome: 'victory' };

              // Auto-advance clock: 1 period per 3 rounds, minimum 1
              const combatRounds = state.activeEncounter.round ?? 1;
              const combatPeriods = Math.max(1, Math.floor(combatRounds / 3));
              const combatClock = advanceClockOnState(state, combatPeriods);
              if (!resolvedTurn.stateChanges.clockAdvance) resolvedTurn.stateChanges.clockAdvance = combatClock.clockAdvance;

              state.activeEncounter = undefined;
          }
      }

  WHY THIS WORKS:
    - syncCombatantsFromState (called just before) sets combatant.defeated = true
      for any NPC whose statBlock.hp <= 0, so allDefeated() returns the correct
      signal even when the turn executor set HP to 0 rather than the GM.
    - The guard !resolvedTurn.stateChanges.encounterEnded ensures we never
      double-process a GM-supplied encounterEnded that applyGMStateChanges
      already handled (state.activeEncounter would already be undefined, but the
      explicit check is belt-and-suspenders).
    - turn.stateChanges is the SAME object reference as resolvedTurn.stateChanges
      (set at turn construction earlier in the function), so mutating
      resolvedTurn.stateChanges here automatically updates the persisted turn
      record without any extra wiring.
    - NPC alive/hp housekeeping mirrors applyGMStateChanges exactly so world
      state is consistent whether encounterEnded came from the GM or auto-close.

  Verification: npx tsc --noEmit â€” 0 new errors (same 5 pre-existing).
  Verification: npx vitest run adventure-turn.test.ts â€” 12 failed | 183 passed;
                same pre-existing failures, zero regressions introduced.


================================================================================
GROUP 23 â€” COMBAT MECHANICS BUG FIXES (Issue 6: reject premature AI victory declaration)
================================================================================
  File: site/src/lib/server/ai/adventure-turn.ts
  Function: sanitizeStateChanges (L1406)
  Issue: #6 â€” AI proposes encounterEnded: { outcome: 'victory' } while
         activeEncounter still has living NPC combatants (HP > 0, not
         defeated). No validation blocked this, so an optimistic AI could
         end an encounter before all enemies were actually killed, skipping
         XP award and leaving state inconsistent.

  Change 23.1 â€” Add premature victory guard in encounterEnded sanitizer block
  Location: ~L1981 in sanitizeStateChanges, the `encounterEnded` validation block
  Before:
    // --- encounterEnded (only if no encounterStarted in same response) ---
    if (sc.encounterEnded && !sc.encounterStarted) {
        if (typeof sc.encounterEnded === 'object' && sc.encounterEnded) {
            clean.encounterEnded = sc.encounterEnded;
        }
    }

  After:
    // --- encounterEnded (only if no encounterStarted in same response) ---
    if (sc.encounterEnded && !sc.encounterStarted) {
        if (typeof sc.encounterEnded === 'object' && sc.encounterEnded) {
            const proposedOutcome = sc.encounterEnded.outcome ?? 'victory';
            if (proposedOutcome === 'victory' && state.activeEncounter) {
                // Reject premature victory: if any NPC combatant still has HP > 0 and is
                // not marked defeated, strip the field. The auto-close logic in
                // persistResolvedTurnAndState (Group 22) handles actual victory once HP
                // changes are applied.
                const hasLivingEnemies = state.activeEncounter.combatants.some(
                    (c) => c.type === 'npc' && !c.defeated && (c.currentHp ?? 1) > 0
                );
                if (hasLivingEnemies) {
                    console.warn(
                        '[sanitize] encounterEnded: victory rejected â€” living NPC combatants still present; auto-close will handle it'
                    );
                } else {
                    clean.encounterEnded = sc.encounterEnded;
                }
            } else {
                clean.encounterEnded = sc.encounterEnded;
            }
        }
    }

  WHY THIS WORKS:
    - The guard only fires for outcome === 'victory' (default when unset).
      Non-victory outcomes â€” 'defeat', 'flee', 'negotiated' â€” pass through
      unconditionally because those are never premature (the party chose them).
    - The check uses (c.currentHp ?? 1) > 0 so that combatants with a null
      currentHp (e.g. freshly created before HP was populated) are treated as
      alive (conservative, avoids false passes).
    - When the guard strips the field, it logs a [sanitize] warn consistent
      with all other sanitizer warnings in the file.
    - Group 22's auto-close runs after HP changes are applied, so the encounter
      still closes correctly on the same turn â€” the AI just loses control over
      the timing and the engine handles it cleanly.
    - No new imports required; uses fields already on ActiveEncounter.Combatant.

  Verification: npx tsc --noEmit â€” 0 new errors (same 5 pre-existing).
  Verification: npx vitest run adventure-turn.test.ts â€” 12 failed | 183 passed;
                same pre-existing failures, zero regressions introduced.

================================================================================
GROUP 25 â€” UI/TEXT FIX: Double period in GM opening preamble
================================================================================
  File: site/src/lib/game/state.ts
  Function: buildOpeningPreamble (~L440)
  Issue: The "notable detail" sentence appended a trailing '.' to ${feature},
         but feature strings from world-bridge.ts already end with a period
         (e.g. "A village of about 500 people."). This produced double periods
         like "A notable detail stands out immediately: A village of about 500
         people.." in the first GM message.

  Change 25.1 â€” Remove trailing period from feature sentence
  Before:
    feature ? `A notable detail stands out immediately: ${feature}.` : ''

  After:
    feature ? `A notable detail stands out immediately: ${feature}` : ''

  WHY: Features are self-contained sentences authored in world-bridge.ts with
       their own terminal punctuation. The template should not add a second
       period. Removing the extra '.' produces grammatically correct output
       for all feature strings regardless of how they end.

  Verification: npx tsc --noEmit â€” 0 new errors (same 5 pre-existing).


================================================================================
GROUP 26 â€” UI/THEME FIX: Theme conformance for all 7 character creation screens
================================================================================
  File: site/src/lib/components/CharacterCreation.svelte
  Scope: <style> block (~L1611â€“2480)
  Issue: The component's CSS had 50+ hardcoded rgba() color values derived from
         arcane-celestial (the default dark theme). On light themes
         (silver-scroll, vellum-quill, sakura-court, frozen-spire) and other
         non-default themes, cards, inputs, buttons, and text became unreadable
         â€” white text on white backgrounds, invisible borders, etc.

  Root cause: All hardcoded values assumed a dark background (using
         rgba(255,255,255,...) for tinting against dark) or hardcoded the
         arcane-celestial accent color (#7c9cff / rgba(124,156,255,...)).

  Fix strategy: Replace ALL hardcoded rgba values with CSS variables that
         are redefined per-theme in app.css under [data-theme='...'] selectors.

  Substitution mapping applied:
    rgba(255,255,255,0.025-0.03)  card/section bg     â†’ var(--surface)
    rgba(255,255,255,0.04-0.05)   hover/input bg      â†’ var(--bg-alt)
    rgba(255,255,255,0.06-0.12)   borders             â†’ var(--border)
    rgba(255,255,255,0.5-0.9)     text                â†’ var(--text) or var(--text-muted)
    rgba(255,255,255,0.25)        placeholder         â†’ var(--text-muted)
    rgba(124,156,255,0.08-0.15)   accent tint bg      â†’ color-mix(in srgb, var(--accent) %, transparent)
    rgba(124,156,255,0.25-0.5)    accent borders      â†’ color-mix(in srgb, var(--accent) %, transparent)
    rgba(124,156,255,0.8-0.9)     accent text         â†’ var(--accent)
    rgba(255,96,96,...) / #ffb0b0 danger colors       â†’ color-mix(in srgb, var(--danger) %, transparent) / var(--danger)
    rgba(255,120,120,...)         danger (step error) â†’ color-mix(in srgb, var(--danger) %, transparent)
    rgba(14,18,28,0.98)           modal shell bg       â†’ var(--bg)  â† most critical fix
    rgba(255,255,255,0.03) step/shell surfaces        â†’ var(--surface)

  Changes 26.1â€“26.50 (exact rules modified by CSS class):
    Shell     : .sidebar-card, .launch-btn, .cc-shell, .cc-header
    Navigation: .step-node, .step-node.active, .step-node.done, .step-node.error,
                .step-line, .step-line.filled, .close-btn
    Errors    : .error-strip, .err-item, .field-error
    Selectors : .option-list, .option-row, .option-row:hover, .option-row.selected,
                .badge, .tag, .tag.accent
    Detail    : .trait-entry, .choice-card, .choice-card:hover, .choice-card.selected,
                .choice-card.flat, .prof-item, .prof-item strong
    Pills     : .pill, .pill:hover, .pill.selected, .pill.accent
    Abilities : .method-btn, .method-btn:hover, .method-btn.selected, .budget-bar,
                .budget-bar.over, .ability-builder-card, .ab-btn, .ab-bonus,
                .dice-rolled s, .pool-chip
    Skills/Gear: .skill-section, .gear-section, .equip-label, .equip-card,
                 .equip-card:hover, .equip-card.selected, .flavor-section
    Identity  : .name-input, .name-input::placeholder, .alignment-cell,
                .alignment-cell:hover, .alignment-cell.selected,
                .backstory-label textarea
    Footer    : .summary-card, .cc-footer border-top, .btn, .btn.primary,
                .btn.secondary
    Responsive: .option-list border-bottom (media query)

  NOT changed (intentionally kept):
    .cc-backdrop background: rgba(4,6,14,0.88) â€” this is the page-dim overlay
      behind the modal, intentionally dark regardless of theme
    .cc-shell box-shadow: 0 32px 80px rgba(0,0,0,0.55) â€” normal drop shadow
    color-mix() already used for drag-over states â€” left as-is

  WHY var(--bg) for cc-shell:
    The modal shell background was rgba(14,18,28,0.98) â€” a near-opaque dark
    blue-black. On light themes this made the entire character creation modal
    appear with a dark background regardless of the selected theme. Changing it
    to var(--bg) makes the modal match the page background for any theme.

  Verification: npx tsc --noEmit â€” 0 new errors (same 5 pre-existing).
  Verification: No rgba(255,255,255,...), rgba(124,156,255,...), rgba(255,96,96,...),
                rgba(255,120,120,...), rgba(14,18,28,...), or #ffb0b0 values
                remain in the style block (confirmed by grep â€” 0 matches).

  GROUP 28 â€” Background Equipment Interactive Choices System
  Date: 2026-04-13
================================================================================

  OVERVIEW
  --------
  Added fully interactive equipment choice panels to the Background selection step
  (Step 3) of CharacterCreation.svelte. 12 of the 13 backgrounds now have
  declarative choice data that drives radio buttons, text boxes, or dual-radio
  combos instead of static item strings. Choices resolve to final inventory items
  at character creation time. Criminal is unchanged (no interactive choices).

  ARCHITECTURE
  ------------
  New type layer (backgrounds.ts):
    - BackgroundChoiceOption { label, description?, items[] }
    - BackgroundChoiceType = 'radio' | 'text' | 'dual-radio'
    - BackgroundEquipmentChoice { id, sectionLabel, prompt, type, required,
        options?, secondId?, secondPrompt?, secondOptions?,
        textMaxWords?, textMaxChars?, textPlaceholder?, optional?,
        fixedItems?, itemNameTemplate?, skipLabel?, orDefaultOption? }
    - BackgroundDefinition gains optional equipmentChoices?: BackgroundEquipmentChoice[]

  New form field (types.ts):
    - CharacterCreateInput gains backgroundEquipmentChoices?: Record<string, string>
    - Form init in CharacterCreation.svelte includes backgroundEquipmentChoices: {}

  Resolution logic (character-creation.ts):
    - New resolveBackgroundEquipment(backgroundDef, choices): string[]
      Starts with backgroundDef.equipment (static items already updated),
      then iterates equipmentChoices and appends resolved items per type:
        radio     â†’ option.items OR itemNameTemplate substitution
        dual-radio â†’ itemNameTemplate with both rank+separation keys substituted
        text      â†’ orDefaultOption match | skipLabel match | itemNameTemplate | fixedItems
    - createCharacter() updated to call resolveBackgroundEquipment() instead of
      using backgroundDef.equipment directly.

  Prop threading:
    - adventures/[id]/+page.svelte: adds `worldCities = $derived(...)` from
      data.state.world.politics.settlements â€” filtered (pop > 0), sorted desc,
      top 5 names. Passed as worldCities={worldCities} to JournalPanel.
    - JournalPanel.svelte: Props gains worldCities?: string[]; destructures it;
      passes {worldCities} to <CharacterCreation>.
    - CharacterCreation.svelte: Props gains worldCities?: string[]; destructured
      with default [].

  UI (CharacterCreation.svelte):
    - Imports type BackgroundChoiceOption from $lib/game/data/backgrounds
    - bgChoiceOptions = $derived.by() â€” injects worldCities as Urchin radio options
    - setBgChoice(id, value) / bgChoice(id) helpers
    - {#if backgroundDef.equipmentChoices?.length} block inserted between the
      Equipment and Feature sections of the background detail pane.
    - Three widget types:
        radio      â€” flex-wrap pill buttons; hides native radio input
        dual-radio â€” two pill groups (rank, then discharge) with secondPrompt sep
        text       â€” <textarea> with live word counter; optional Or: pill below
    - "No options available â€” a world must be loaded." shown for empty city list.
    - bgChoices validation errors displayed via fieldError('bgChoices') near bottom.

  Validation (CharacterCreation.svelte):
    - getStepFields(2) now returns ['background', 'bgChoices']
    - validateStep(2) loops backgroundDef.equipmentChoices:
        required radio/dual-radio â†’ pushes to 'bgChoices' if empty
        dual-radio secondId       â†’ same check on secondId key
        text textMaxWords        â†’ word-count overage blocked
    - All errors keyed to 'bgChoices' so they surface in step-error count.

  CSS added (CharacterCreation.svelte <style>):
    .bg-choice-section   â€” flex-col gap container for each choice block
    .bg-choice-options   â€” flex-wrap row of pills
    .bg-choice-pill      â€” styled label; .selected = accent tint border/bg
    .bg-choice-pill input[type='radio'] â€” display:none (visual-only select)
    .choice-label        â€” 0.82rem text
    .choice-desc         â€” 0.72rem italic muted (option description)
    .bg-text-input       â€” full-width textarea, var(--bg-alt) background
    .bg-text-input.optional-input â€” opacity 0.72
    .bg-choice-or-row    â€” flex row for "Or:" + pill
    .hint-small          â€” 0.78rem muted sub-hint
    .char-counter        â€” right-aligned word counter; .over = danger color
    .field-error-inline  â€” 0.75rem danger text below required choices
    .hint.muted          â€” reduced opacity variant for "no world loaded" note

  OVERVIEW

       height ranges, skin tones, hair colours/styles, society types, and
       common career paths.

  ensure HMR had applied all races.ts changes from Group 28.

    - Added new field: shortDescription: string

      to `{race.shortDescription}` on the `.option-sub` span
    - Detail pane `<p class="detail-desc">` unchanged â€” still uses
      `{raceDef.description}` which now renders the expanded text

================================================================================
  GROUP 30 â€” Rogue Expertise Player-Choice UI (Issue 1 Fix)
  Date: 2026-04-15
================================================================================

  OVERVIEW
  --------
  Rogue level 1 (and any future class with an 'expertise' tag on a level-1
  feature) now prompts the player to choose 2 skill proficiencies for Expertise
  during character creation. Previously, `expertiseSkills` was always set to
  `[]` in createCharacter(). Now the player makes the choice in a new UI
  section on the Step 5 "Magic & Starting Equipment" screen, and their choices
  are validated and stored on the resulting PlayerCharacter.

  RULE ENFORCED
  -------------
  - Player must pick exactly 2 skills for expertise.
  - Only skills the character is already proficient in (from class, background,
    race fixed skills, or bonus picks) are offered.
  - 'thieves-tools' is not in the expertise pool â€” the UI restricts to SkillName
    only (tools-as-expertise is a future enhancement).
  - Non-rogue classes show no expertise section (expertiseCount derives to 0).
  - The section is hidden entirely when expertiseCount === 0.

  FILES MODIFIED (4 files)
  ------------------------

  1. src/lib/game/types.ts
     Interface: CharacterCreateInput
     Change: Added new optional field after `variantHumanFeat`:
       /** Expertise skill choices for classes with the Expertise feature
           (e.g. Rogue level 1). */
       expertiseChoices?: SkillName[];

  2. src/lib/game/character-creation.ts
     Function: validateCharacterInput()
     Change: Added call to validateExpertise(input, errors) after
       validateEquipment().

     New function added (before Feature-use map section):
       function validateExpertise(input, errors):
         - Gets classDef, checks for level-1 feature with tag 'expertise'.
         - If not present, returns early (non-expertise classes pass silently).
         - Rebuilds skillProficiencies from background + race + bonusSkills +
           chosenSkills (same logic as createCharacter).
         - Validates: choices.length === 2.
         - Validates: no duplicate choices (Set size check).
         - Validates: every choice is in skillProficiencies.

     Function: createCharacter()
     Change: Replaced `expertiseSkills: [],` with computed value.
       Before the return object, added:
         const hasExpertiseFeature = classDef features.some(
           f => f.level === 1 && f.tags.includes('expertise')
         );
         const expertiseSkills: SkillName[] = hasExpertiseFeature
           ? Array.from(new Set(input.expertiseChoices ?? []))
               .filter(c => skillProficiencies.includes(c))
               .slice(0, 2)
           : [];
       In the return object: expertiseSkills is now the variable (not []).

  3. src/lib/components/CharacterCreation.svelte
     Form init:
       Added `expertiseChoices: []` to the $state form initialiser
       (after backgroundEquipmentChoices: {}).

     New $derived values (after pointBuySummary):
       let expertiseCount = $derived(
         classDef?.features.some(f => f.level === 1 && f.tags.includes
         ('expertise')) ? 2 : 0
       );
       let expertisePool = $derived(
         Array.from(new Set([...backgroundSkills, ...fixedRacialSkills,
           ...(form.bonusSkillChoices ?? []), ...form.chosenSkills]))
         as SkillName[]
       );

     New function (after toggleSpell):
       function toggleExpertise(skill: SkillName):
         - Deselects if already chosen.
         - Refuses to exceed expertiseCount.
         - Appends to form.expertiseChoices.

     getStepFields(5): 'expertiseChoices' added as first entry:
       return ['expertiseChoices', 'spellChoices', 'spellChoices.cantrips',
         'spellChoices.knownSpells', 'spellChoices.preparedSpells',
         'equipmentSelections'];

     validateStep(step === 5): New check added as first guard:
       if (expertiseCount > 0 &&
           (form.expertiseChoices ?? []).length !== expertiseCount) {
         issues.push({ field: 'expertiseChoices',
           message: `Choose ${expertiseCount} skills for expertise.` });
       }

     Step 5 template: New gear-section block inserted immediately after
     the `<h3 class="section-title">` and before the spell-choices block:
       {#if expertiseCount > 0}
         <div class="gear-section">
           <h4>Expertise</h4>
           <div class="spell-group">
             <div class="spell-group-header">
               <span>Choose {expertiseCount} skills to double your proficiency
                 bonus</span>
               <span class="counter">{chosen}/{expertiseCount}</span>
             </div>
             <div class="pill-row">
               {#each expertisePool as skill}
                 <button pill class:selected={...} onclick={toggleExpertise}>
                   {formatLabel(skill)}
                 </button>
               {/each}
             </div>
             {#if fieldError('expertiseChoices')}
               <p class="field-error">...</p>
             {/if}
           </div>
         </div>
       {/if}

     CSS: No new CSS required. Reuses .gear-section, .spell-group,
       .spell-group-header, .counter, .pill-row, .pill, .pill.selected,
       .field-error â€” all already defined in the component.

  VERIFICATION
  ------------

  Files changed: types.ts, character-creation.ts, CharacterCreation.svelte.
  Rogue creates with expertiseSkills populated from player choices.

================================================================================
  GROUP 31 â€” Weapon Proficiency SRD Audit & Unarmed Strike (Issue 2 Fix)
  Date: 2026-04-15
================================================================================

  OVERVIEW
  --------
  Full SRD audit of all 12 class weapon proficiency arrays. Six classes had
  incorrect or missing weapon proficiencies compared to the SRD. All have been
  corrected. Universal unarmed strike proficiency (per SRD PHB p.195) is now
  automatically added to every new character's weaponProficiencies array during
  character creation.

  KEY DESIGN DECISIONS
  --------------------
  - 'simple' and 'martial' remain as umbrella category strings (the AI/GM
    context understands them as "proficient with ALL weapons in that category").
  - Classes with partial category access (Wizard, Sorcerer, Druid) now use
    explicit individual weapon name strings instead of the category umbrella.
  - Classes with full simple + select martial extras (Rogue, Bard, Monk) use
    'simple' plus the specific martial weapon names.
  - 'unarmed' is injected first in the Set in createCharacter(), so it always
    appears as the first entry (before class/race additions). Improvised weapons
    are intentionally NOT added to any class's proficiency list.
  - WeaponProficiency type in races.ts expanded so all individual weapon name
    strings are valid TypeScript types on the ClassDefinition arrays.

  SRD WEAPON PROFICIENCY REFERENCE (5e SRD CC-BY-4.0)
  ----------------------------------------------------
  Simple Melee:   club, dagger, greatclub, handaxe, javelin, light-hammer,
                  mace, quarterstaff, sickle, spear
  Simple Ranged:  dart, light-crossbow, shortbow, sling
  Martial Melee:  battleaxe, flail, glaive, greataxe, greatsword, halberd,
                  lance, longsword, maul, morningstar, pike, rapier, scimitar,
                  shortsword, trident, war-pick, warhammer, whip
  Martial Ranged: blowgun, hand-crossbow, heavy-crossbow, longbow, net
  Special:        unarmed (universal â€” all creatures)

  AUDIT RESULTS (12 classes)
  --------------------------
  Fighter   ['simple','martial']             âœ… Correct â€” no change
  Wizard    ['dagger','dart','sling',        âœ… FIXED (was [])
              'quarterstaff','light-crossbow']
  Rogue     ['simple','hand-crossbow',       âœ… FIXED (was ['simple'])
              'longsword','rapier','shortsword']
  Cleric    ['simple']                       âœ… Correct â€” no change
  Ranger    ['simple','martial']             âœ… Correct â€” no change
  Barbarian ['simple','martial']             âœ… Correct â€” no change
  Bard      ['simple','hand-crossbow',       âœ… FIXED (was ['simple'])
              'longsword','rapier','shortsword']
  Paladin   ['simple','martial']             âœ… Correct â€” no change
  Sorcerer  ['dagger','dart','sling',        âœ… FIXED (was [])
              'quarterstaff','light-crossbow']
  Warlock   ['simple']                       âœ… Correct â€” no change
  Druid     ['club','dagger','dart',         âœ… FIXED (was [])
              'javelin','mace','quarterstaff',
              'scimitar','sickle','sling','spear']
  Monk      ['simple','shortsword']          âœ… FIXED (was ['simple'])

  FILES MODIFIED (3 files)
  ------------------------

  1. src/lib/game/data/races.ts
     Type: WeaponProficiency
     Change: Expanded from 10 specific weapon names to all 39 weapon names

     Before:

     After: Full categorised union covering all simple melee, simple ranged,

================================================================================
  GROUP 32 â€” Starting Equipment System Fix (Issue 3 Fix)
  Date: April 15, 2026
================================================================================

  PROBLEM STATEMENT
  -----------------
  Characters were created with missing starting inventory items. Root cause
  analysis revealed an architectural gap: ClassDefinition only had
  equipmentChoices (player pick-one-of-several selections) but NO field for
  "guaranteed" items every class member always receives. A legacy function
  starterEquipment() in world-bridge.ts contained correct per-class data but
  was NEVER called â€” dead code from a prototype that was never integrated.

  Example: A Rogue always receives Leather Armor, two Daggers, and Thieves'
  Tools in addition to their weapon/pack choices. None of these appeared in
  any character's inventory because the creation system had no mechanism to
  grant automatic items. 10 of 12 classes were affected.

  ROOT CAUSE (Technical)
  ----------------------
  resolveStartingEquipment() in character-creation.ts only read:
    classDef?.equipmentChoices â†’ player selections (pick A or B)
  It did not read any "guaranteed" items field because none existed on
  ClassDefinition. The starterEquipment() function in world-bridge.ts was
  never wired into createCharacter().

  CHANGES MADE
  ------------

  --- FILE: site/src/lib/game/data/classes.ts ---

  [1] ClassDefinition interface â€” added startingEquipment field:
    Before:
      equipmentChoices: StartingEquipmentChoice[];
      /** Multiclass prerequisites ... */
      multiclassPrereqs: AbilityName[];
    After:
      equipmentChoices: StartingEquipmentChoice[];
      /** Guaranteed items received at character creation, regardless of
          player equipment choices. */
      startingEquipment: string[];
      /** Multiclass prerequisites ... */
      multiclassPrereqs: AbilityName[];

  [2] All 12 class definitions â€” added startingEquipment arrays:
    Fighter:    startingEquipment: []
    Wizard:     startingEquipment: []
    Rogue:      startingEquipment: ['Leather Armor', 'Two Daggers', "Thieves' Tools"]
    Cleric:     startingEquipment: ['Shield', 'Holy Symbol']
    Ranger:     startingEquipment: ['Longbow', 'Arrows (20)']
    Barbarian:  startingEquipment: ['Four Javelins']
    Bard:       startingEquipment: ['Leather Armor']
    Paladin:    startingEquipment: ['Chain Mail', 'Holy Symbol']
    Sorcerer:   startingEquipment: ['Two Daggers']
    Warlock:    startingEquipment: ['Leather Armor', 'Two Daggers']
    Druid:      startingEquipment: ['Leather Armor', 'Druidic Focus']
    Monk:       startingEquipment: ['Dart (10)']
  All values verified against D&D 5e SRD. 10 of 12 classes had missing items.
  Fighter and Wizard have no automatic items under SRD rules.

  --- FILE: site/src/lib/game/character-creation.ts ---

  [3] resolveStartingEquipment() â€” spread class guaranteed items into labels:
    Before:
      const labels = [...selectedRows.flat(), ...backgroundEquipment];
    After:
      const labels = [
        ...selectedRows.flat(),
        ...(classDef?.startingEquipment ?? []),
        ...backgroundEquipment
      ];
    DESIGN NOTE: startingEquipment is positioned AFTER selectedRows.flat() so
    that index === 0 (equipPrimary = true) still applies to the player's first
    CHOSEN weapon, not an automatic item. Armor items auto-equip regardless of
    position via itemFromLabel()'s armor branch. All string labels resolve
    through the existing itemFromLabel() pipeline:
      'Leather Armor' / 'Chain Mail' / 'Shield' â†’ getArmor() â†’ auto-equipped
      'Two Daggers' / 'Four Javelins' â†’ WORD_QUANTITY_PREFIX â†’ getWeapon()
      'Dart (10)' / 'Arrows (20)' â†’ parseItemLabel() qty parsing
      "Thieves' Tools" / 'Holy Symbol' / 'Druidic Focus' â†’ getGear()

  --- FILE: site/src/lib/components/CharacterCreation.svelte ---

  [4] Step 5 (Magic & Starting Equipment) â€” added Guaranteed Equipment section:
    Added after the existing {#if classDef?.equipmentChoices.length} block
    (which shows player choice cards), before the pane-content closing </div>:
      {#if classDef?.startingEquipment && classDef.startingEquipment.length > 0}
        <div class="gear-section">
          <h4>Guaranteed Equipment</h4>
          <p class="equip-guaranteed-note">Every {classDef.displayName}
            starts with these automatically.</p>
          <div class="equip-options">
            {#each classDef.startingEquipment as item}
              <span class="pill selected">{item}</span>
            {/each}
          </div>
        </div>
      {/if}
    Also added CSS rule:
      .equip-guaranteed-note {
        font-size: 0.82rem;
        color: var(--text-muted);
        margin: 0;
      }
    The block uses existing .gear-section, .equip-options, and .pill.selected
    CSS classes. Items render as read-only badges (non-interactive).

  --- FILE: site/src/lib/game/world-bridge.ts ---

  [5] starterEquipment() â€” marked deprecated:
    Changed JSDoc comment from:
      /** Generate starting equipment for a character based on their class. */
    To:
      /**
       * Generate starting equipment for a character based on their class.
       * @deprecated Superseded by ClassDefinition.startingEquipment +
       *   resolveStartingEquipment() in character-creation.ts.
       *   This function is no longer called; preserved for reference only.
       */
    Function body is UNCHANGED. Not deleted â€” preserved as SRD reference.

  ITEM STRING RESOLUTION VERIFIED
  --------------------------------
  All startingEquipment string labels were verified to pass through
  itemFromLabel() correctly before implementation:
    'Leather Armor'    â†’ getArmor('leather armor')    â†’ ArmorItem, baseAC 11
    'Chain Mail'       â†’ getArmor('chain mail')        â†’ ArmorItem, baseAC 16
    'Shield'           â†’ getArmor('shield')            â†’ ArmorItem (shield type)
    'Two Daggers'      â†’ WORD_QUANTITY_PREFIX('two ')  â†’ getWeapon('dagger'), qty 2
    'Four Javelins'    â†’ WORD_QUANTITY_PREFIX('four ') â†’ getWeapon('javelin'), qty 4
    'Longbow'          â†’ getWeapon('longbow')          â†’ WeaponItem
    'Arrows (20)'      â†’ parseItemLabel â†’ baseName='Arrows', qty=20 â†’ misc
    "Thieves' Tools"   â†’ getGear by displayName        â†’ GearItem
    'Holy Symbol'      â†’ getGear by displayName        â†’ GearItem
    'Druidic Focus'    â†’ getGear by displayName        â†’ GearItem
    'Dart (10)'        â†’ parseItemLabel â†’ baseName='Dart', qty=10 â†’ getWeapon

  VERIFICATION
  ------------
  npx tsc --noEmit: Same 5 pre-existing errors only. 0 new errors.
  Files changed: classes.ts, character-creation.ts, CharacterCreation.svelte,
    world-bridge.ts.

================================================================================
  GROUP 33 â€” NPC Duplicate Fix + Alias System (Issues 4â€“8)
  Date: April 16, 2026
================================================================================

  PROBLEM STATEMENT
  -----------------
  Five separate issues were found in the Testing.JSON adventure save for
  Steel-Jaw's campaign (Jtest 4), all stemming from the same root cause:
  the AI had no mechanism to recognise that an NPC it already knew by one name
  might be referred to by a different name.

  Issue 4: npc-001 (Tessara) and npc-002 (Aunt Tess) were the same person â€”
    Steel-Jaw's elderly aunt in Kaara Reach â€” tracked as two separate NPCs.
    Tessara was created at turn 5 (formal recognition). Aunt Tess was created
    at turn 23 when the player addressed her informally. npc-002 carried the
    wrong locationId ("The Wilds Near Kaara Reach") despite the encounter
    taking place in the village.

  Issue 5: All of Aunt Tess's notes (turns 23-118) were stored under npc-002
    and isolated from Tessara's notes (turns 5-7), fragmenting her history.
    The AI only ever saw 2 lines of history for the character instead of 8.

  Issue 6: Three interaction notes for npc-002 (turns 23, 25, 28) contained
    the name "Jareth" â€” a ghost name for a character that does not exist in
    this campaign. The AI likely invented the name while writing notes, sourced
    from the wrong context.

  Issue 7: Hilden's interactionNotes had two exact duplicates:
    - Turn 104: two nearly-identical notes ("Steel-Jaw informed Hilden..." and
      "Hilden is informed by Steel-Jaw...") â€” state extraction ran twice.
    - Turn 106: two word-for-word identical notes for the same event.


  Issue 8: Xilara's locationId was "loc-hidden-meeting-point" (Hidden Glade).
    She had since traveled to Kaara Reach for the diplomatic meeting (turns
    104-121) but the location was never updated in state.

  ROOT CAUSE (Shared)
  -------------------
  The NPC type had no aliases field. The AI prompt showed:
    [name: Tessara][id: npc-001] (neutral, warm)
  When the player typed "Aunt Tess", the AI saw no link to npc-001 and created
  npc-002. The system is entirely ID-based with no fuzzy name matching, so
  context visibility is the only prevention mechanism.

  CHANGES MADE
  ------------

  --- FILE: project-zeus/Testing.JSON (adventure save â€” state.npcs) ---

    description:        "An elderly woman..." â†’
                        "Steel-Jaw's aunt; an elderly woman with a gentle and
                         reassuring presence, familiar from his childhood in
                         Kaara Reach."
    lastInteractionTurn: 9 â†’ 118
    aliases (new):      ["Aunt Tess", "Auntie"]
    interactionNotes:   2 notes â†’ 8 notes (merged chronologically and Jareth
                        references corrected):
      turn 5:  (kept) "Steel-Jaw recognized Tessara..."
      turn 7:  (kept) "Tessara discussed the village's events..."
      turn 23: (from npc-002, fixed) "Tessara's defensive vigilance melted away
               upon recognizing Steel-Jaw. Deep relief and joy at their reunion.
               She welcomed Steel-Jaw back warmly."
               (was: "Jareth's defensive vigilance melted away...")
      turn 25: (from npc-002, fixed) "Tessara was happy to see Steel-Jaw had
               returned and suggested a good meal to clear heads and prepare for
               tasks ahead."
               (was: "...and Jareth suggests a good meal...")
      turn 28: (from npc-002, fixed) "Steel-Jaw arrived at Tessara's dwelling."
               (was: "Jareth and Steel-Jaw arrived at Aunt Tess's dwelling.")
      turn 66: (from npc-002, kept) "Awakened by Steel-Jaw using dragonborn
               scale dust..."
      turn 111: (from npc-002, updated name) "Tessara has a soft spot for
                Cheese despite her mock sternness."
      turn 118: (from npc-002, kept) "Steel-Jaw successfully used the stones..."

      alive: boolean;
    After:

      notes: string;

          prevent duplicate NPC creation. */
      aliases?: string[];
      alive: boolean;

  --- FILE: site/src/lib/game/gm-context.ts ---

  [6] KNOWN NPCs rendering â€” append aliases to NPC line:
    In the loop that renders remote NPCs (KNOWN NPCs section), added aliasStr:
    Before:
      parts.push(`  - ${formatNameIdRef(n.name, n.id)} (${n.role},
        ${dispositionLabel(n.disposition)})${summaryStr}`);
    After:

        ? ` (also known as: ${n.aliases.join(', ')})` : '';
      parts.push(`  - ${formatNameIdRef(n.name, n.id)} (${n.role},
        ${dispositionLabel(n.disposition)})${aliasStr}${summaryStr}`);
    Effect: Tessara now renders as:
      [name: Tessara][id: npc-001] (neutral, warm) (also known as: Aunt Tess,
      Auntie) â€” Steel-Jaw recognized Tessara...

  [7] GM pass extraction rule â€” added alias-check guard (line ~440):
    Before:
      - Every NPC you mention by name for the FIRST TIME must be tracked via
        npcsAdded. Do not introduce named NPCs only in narrative.
    After (added following line):
      - Before adding a new NPC via npcsAdded, check KNOWN NPCs for any
        existing entry showing "(also known as: ...)" â€” if the name matches an
        alias, use that NPC's existing id rather than creating a duplicate.

  [8] State-extraction pass rule â€” updated npcsAdded guideline (line ~502):
    Before:
      - If the narrative mentions a new NPC by name, you MUST emit npcsAdded.
    After:
      - If the narrative mentions a new NPC by name, you MUST emit npcsAdded â€”
        unless the name matches an alias shown in parentheses after any existing
        KNOWN NPC entry (e.g. "(also known as: Aunt Tess)"), in which case use
        that NPC's existing id instead.

  VERIFICATION
  ------------
  npx tsc --noEmit: Same 5 pre-existing errors only. 0 new errors.
  Files changed: Testing.JSON, types.ts, gm-context.ts.
  Issues resolved: 4, 5, 6, 7, 8.

================================================================================
  GROUP 34 â€” Quest Resolution System (Phases 1â€“5)
  Date: April 17, 2026
================================================================================

  PROBLEM STATEMENT
  -----------------
  The quest system had no way to differentiate HOW a quest was resolved.
  A "defeat-encounter" objective could never be completed by diplomacy â€”
  the objective type was treated as the only resolution path. Quests also had
  no stakes (no failure consequences visible to the AI), no deadlines, and
  no chain infrastructure (no follow-up quest wiring).

  Root cause (Issue 9 context): A main quest with a "defeat" objective remained
  stuck even after the party successfully negotiated a diplomatic resolution,
  because the engine expected combat completion only. The AI had no mechanism
  to record that diplomacy was the resolution method, and the GM prompt gave
  no instruction to allow alternative methods.

  DESIGN GOALS
  ------------
  1. Any quest objective can be completed by any valid resolution method.
  2. The AI records how a quest was resolved (completionMethod).
  3. Active quests with stakes show their failureConsequence to the AI.
  4. Time-sensitive quests auto-fail when their deadline passes.
  5. Completed quests activate follow-up quests (followUpQuestIds).
  6. Quest chains are browsable in both directions (follow-ups + prerequisites).

  CHANGES MADE
  ------------

  --- PHASE 1: site/src/lib/game/types.ts ---

  [1] Added QuestCompletionMethod type (before Quest interface):
      export type QuestCompletionMethod =
        'combat' | 'diplomacy' | 'stealth' | 'bribery' |
        'deception' | 'custom' | 'expired';
      Values: combat (defeated in battle), diplomacy (negotiated/talked-down),
      stealth (bypassed unseen), bribery (paid off), deception (tricked),
      custom (other), expired (engine-set when deadline passes).

  [2] Quest interface â€” added 5 new optional fields (after encounterTemplates):
      completionMethod?: QuestCompletionMethod
        â€” how quest resolved; engine sets on status â†’ completed/failed.
      deadline?: { day: number; description: string }
        â€” auto-fails when state.clock.day > deadline.day.
      failureConsequence?: string
        â€” stakes reminder shown to AI every turn for active quests.
      followUpQuestIds?: GameId[]
        â€” quests made 'available' when this quest completes.
      prerequisiteQuestIds?: GameId[]
        â€” quests that must be 'completed' before this can become 'active'.

  [3] StateChange.questUpdates â€” added completionMethod field:
      Before: Array<{ questId, field, oldValue, newValue, objectiveId? }>
      After:  Array<{ ...same..., completionMethod?: QuestCompletionMethod }>
      AI includes this when field === 'status' and resolving/failing a quest.

  [4] StateChange.questsAdded â€” added 4 new optional fields:
      failureConsequence?: string
      deadline?: { day: number; description: string }
      followUpQuestIds?: GameId[]
      prerequisiteQuestIds?: GameId[]

  --- PHASE 2: site/src/lib/game/gm-context.ts ---

  [5] buildGameStateContextBlock â€” QUESTS section rendering enhanced:
      For active quests, appended per-quest to each line (when set):
        âš  Consequence if failed: <failureConsequence>
        Deadline: Day <N> â€” <description>
        Unlocks: [name][id:...] list (followUpQuestIds resolved to names)
        Requires: [name][id:...] list (prerequisiteQuestIds resolved to names)

  [6] buildSystemPrompt â€” questUpdates schema updated:
      Added "completionMethod": "combat|diplomacy|stealth|bribery|deception|custom
      (include when completing or failing)" to the status variant.

  [7] buildSystemPrompt â€” questsAdded schema updated:
      Added failureConsequence, deadline, and followUpQuestIds optional fields
      to the quest schema description.

  [8] buildSystemPrompt â€” CRITICAL RULES section appended two new rules:
      QUEST COMPLETION METHOD: Explains that completionMethod is required when
        changing quest status, lists all valid values, explicitly states that
        "defeat-encounter" objectives CAN be resolved by diplomacy.
      QUEST STAKES: Instructs the AI to add failureConsequence and deadline
        when creating new quests to create reactive narrative stakes.

  [9] buildStateExtractionPrompt â€” questUpdates schema updated:
      Expanded the single-line "field: status|objective" description to match
      the buildSystemPrompt schema, including completionMethod field.

  [10] buildStateExtractionPrompt â€” questsAdded schema updated:
       Added same failureConsequence, deadline, and followUpQuestIds fields.

  [11] buildStateExtractionPrompt â€” IMPORTANT GUIDELINES appended:
       QUEST COMPLETION METHOD guideline mirrors the buildSystemPrompt rule,
       ensuring the extraction AI also captures method on all resolutions.

  [12] buildStateExtractionPrompt â€” QUESTS state snapshot enhanced:
       For active quests, appended failureConsequence and deadline to each line
       (same format as buildGameStateContextBlock) so the extraction AI sees
       the same stake/deadline information the narrative AI saw.

  --- PHASE 3: site/src/lib/server/ai/adventure-turn.ts ---

  [13] applyGMStateChanges â€” questsAdded Phase A block:
       Now passes failureConsequence, deadline, followUpQuestIds, and
       prerequisiteQuestIds from qData onto the constructed Quest object.

  [14] applyGMStateChanges â€” questUpdates field:'status' handler:
       Three additions:
       a) Stores quest.completionMethod = qu.completionMethod (when present).
       b) On completion: activates followUpQuestIds quests (sets them to
          'available' if not already active/completed), then pushes
          extend-quest-arc enrichment intent.
       c) On failure: pushes a sceneFactsAdded entry with quest failureConsequence
          text: "Quest '<name>' failed: <consequence>"

  [15] applyGMStateChanges â€” objective auto-completion handler:
       Added followUpQuestIds activation (same logic as [14b]) when all
       objectives are done and quest auto-completes.
       Also removed the now-incorrect `if (quest.status !== 'completed')` guard
       that TypeScript (correctly) flagged as always-true after narrowing.

  [16] applyGMStateChanges â€” new Deadline Enforcement section (end of function):
       After all other processing, loops over active quests with a deadline.
       If state.clock.day > quest.deadline.day:
         quest.status = 'failed'
         quest.completionMethod = 'expired'
         Pushes scene fact: "Quest '<name>' expired (Day <N>): <consequence>"
         or a plain note if no failureConsequence set.

  --- PHASE 4: site/src/lib/server/ai/world-enrichment.ts ---

  [17] systemPrompt() â€” appended quest schema guidance:
       Added paragraph explaining failureConsequence, deadline, followUpQuestIds,
       and prerequisiteQuestIds as optional quest fields AI may include.

  [18] parseEnrichmentResponse() â€” questsAdded parser:
       Added parsing for failureConsequence (string, trimmed), deadline (object
       with day:number and description:string validated), followUpQuestIds
       (string array, filtered), and prerequisiteQuestIds (string array, filtered).
       All fields are optional and undefined when absent/invalid.

  [19] extendQuestArc() â€” return JSON schema updated:
       Added failureConsequence, deadline, and followUpQuestIds to the template
       JSON the AI is asked to return when generating follow-up quests.

  --- PHASE 5: site/src/trigger/world-enrichment.ts ---

  [20] applyEnrichmentChanges() â€” questsAdded block:
       Now passes failureConsequence, deadline, followUpQuestIds, and
       prerequisiteQuestIds from qData onto the constructed Quest object
       (mirrors the Phase 3 change to applyGMStateChanges).

  [21] extendQuestArcTask run handler:
       After applyEnrichmentChanges, if result.stateChanges.questsAdded has
       entries, finds the source quest by questId and adds all new quest IDs
       to sourceQuest.followUpQuestIds (creating the array if needed).
       This bi-directional link means the quest chain is browsable from either
       end, and gm-context.ts will show "Unlocks: [new quest]" on the source.

  SYSTEM INTERACTION SUMMARY
  --------------------------
  Turn flow with new system:
  1. Player resolves quest by diplomacy instead of combat.
  2. AI emits questUpdates: { field:'status', newValue:'completed',
     completionMethod:'diplomacy' }.
  3. Engine stores quest.completionMethod = 'diplomacy'.
  4. Engine activates any followUpQuestIds (sets them to 'available').
  5. Engine pushes extend-quest-arc enrichment intent.
  6. Background task generates follow-up quest and links it back to source.

  Deadline flow:
  1. Quest created with deadline: { day: 10, description: "Bandits leave area" }.
  2. Each turn, after all changes, deadline sweep runs.
  3. On day 11 with quest still active: quest.status = 'failed',
     completionMethod = 'expired', scene fact emitted with failureConsequence.
  4. AI sees the scene fact on subsequent turns and narrates consequences.

  Failure consequence flow:
  1. Quest created with failureConsequence: "The cult completes its ritual."
  2. Every turn, AI sees: âš  Consequence if failed: The cult completes its ritual.
  3. If quest fails: engine pushes "Quest 'X' failed: The cult completes..." fact.
  4. Fact persists in sceneFacts and shows in all subsequent AI context.

  VERIFICATION
  ------------
  npx tsc --noEmit: Same 4 pre-existing errors only (combat.ts, gm-context.ts,
    turn-executor.ts Ã—2). Zero new errors introduced.
  Files changed: types.ts, gm-context.ts, adventure-turn.ts,
    world-enrichment.ts (lib), world-enrichment.ts (trigger).

================================================================================
  GROUP 35 â€” Settlement System Overhaul ("Show, Don't Tell")
  Date: April 17, 2026
================================================================================

  PROBLEM STATEMENT
  -----------------
  The settlement system produced immersion-breaking output in three ways:

  1. Settlement `group` (hamlet/village/town/city) was assigned at random
     during world generation, with no correlation to population size.
     A "city" could have 400 people; a "hamlet" could have 25,000.

  2. `buildSettlementDescription()` used a single template for all
     settlement tiers: "${name} is a ${group} nestled in the lands of..."
     Every location sounded identical â€” no architectural character, no
     sensory detail, no tier differentiation.

  3. The features array (shown to the AI every turn) hardcoded a population
     count: "A village of about 22,680 people." â€” AI would then narrate
     population census data instead of scene details.

  4. `buildWorldBrief()` injected "a ${group} of ${pop * 1000} people"
     into the AI system prompt on every turn, compounding the census problem.

  5. `seedStartingLocation()` explicitly EXCLUDED cities from consideration,
     so players never started in the largest, most content-rich settlement.

  6. `expandSettlement()` had no instruction to avoid population numbers or
     tier-label words in its AI-generated NPC and scene-fact output.

  DESIGN GOALS
  ------------
  1. Group derived from population â€” no random assignment.
  2. Four unique description templates (hamlet/village/town/city) with
     terrain-type variation (River/Naval/Highland/Generic) â€” "show, don't tell."
  3. Features array: architectural and cultural cues only â€” no population count.
  4. AI system prompt: size label ("a walled city") not census number.
  5. New adventures always start at the largest city (most hooks, most NPCs).
  6. AI enrichment prompt: explicitly forbids population numbers and tier words
     in description text.

  CHANGES MADE
  ------------

  --- PHASE 1: site/src/lib/worldgen/prototype.ts ---

  Settlement generation â€” group derived from population (not random pick):

  BEFORE (in Array.from settlements block, ~line 206):
      group: pick(rng, ['hamlet', 'village', 'town', 'city'])

  AFTER:
      const population = float(rng, 0.2, 28, 3);
      const group =
          population < 0.5  ? 'hamlet'  :
          population < 2.0  ? 'village' :
          population < 8.0  ? 'town'    : 'city';
      // population and group used in the settlement object literal below

  Population thresholds (Ã— 1,000):
      hamlet  < 500
      village < 2,000
      town    < 8,000
      city    â‰¥ 8,000

  --- PHASE 2: site/src/lib/game/world-bridge.ts ---

  [A] seedStartingLocation() â€” prefer largest city

  BEFORE:
      const candidates = world.politics.settlements
          .filter((s) => s.group === 'village' || s.group === 'town')
          .filter((s) => !s.capital);
      const pick = candidates.length > 0 ? candidates[0] : world.politics.settlements[0];

  AFTER:
      const byPopDesc = (a, b) => b.population - a.population;
      const cities = world.politics.settlements.filter((s) => s.group === 'city').sort(byPopDesc);
      const towns  = world.politics.settlements.filter((s) => s.group === 'town').sort(byPopDesc);
      const pick =
          cities.length > 0 ? cities[0] :
          towns.length  > 0 ? towns[0]  :
          world.politics.settlements.slice().sort(byPopDesc)[0];
      // removed capital-exclusion filter â€” capital cities are fine starting points

  [B] buildSettlementDescription() â€” full rewrite with 4 tier templates

  Replaced the single "nestled in the lands of" template with four
  distinct descriptions keyed on settlement.group, each with a terrain
  variation line keyed on settlement.type (River/Naval/Highland/Generic).

  Template structure per tier:
    hamlet  â€” "a name on a map more than a place" â€” no walls, well, woodsmoke,
              shrine if religion exists.
    village â€” "exists because the road stops here for the night" â€” palisade,
              market square, customs, polite caution, open shrine.

              guild-day square, contracts matter, authority banner.
    city    â€” "rises behind stone walls" â€” outer curtain, layered districts
              (merchant / artisan / civic), faith towers, old families.

  Terrain variation lines (applied to all tiers):
    River   â€” "The ${riverName} cuts along its edge, busy with flat-bottomed
               trading barges." (falls back if no named river)
    Naval   â€” "Stone quays face the harbour mouth..."
    Highland â€” "The approach road climbs steeply..."
    Generic â€” "The main road from ${stateName} passes directly through..."

  Faith reference added at end if state has a religion.

  [C] buildSettlementFeatures() â€” new helper function

  Added immediately after buildSettlementDescription(). Returns string[]
  of architectural/cultural cues â€” NO population count anywhere.

  Features by tier:
    hamlet  â€” "No walls or defences â€” cluster of buildings around a central well."
    village â€” "Market square with a well; weekly stalls..."
              "Low wooden palisade marks the boundary..."
    town    â€” "Earthwork outer wall with watched gates..."
              "Market square large enough for guild days..."
    city    â€” "Stone curtain walls; outer gate checked by guards..."
              "Multiple merchant, artisan, and civic districts within the walls."

  Additional lines appended conditionally:
    River/Naval/Highland â€” terrain/water feature line
    state exists         â€” "Under ${state.fullName} authority."
    culture exists       â€” "${culture.name} customs govern trade..."
    religion exists      â€” "${religion.name} faith has a presence here..."

  [D] Both features arrays updated to use buildSettlementFeatures()

  In seedStartingLocation():

            `A ${pick.group} of about ${Math.round(pick.population * 1000)
                .toLocaleString('en')} people.`,
            ownerState ? `Under the rule of ${ownerState.fullName}.` : '',

        ].filter(Boolean),

    AFTER:

  In seedNearbyLocations() loc literal â€” same change (same BEFORE/AFTER pattern).

  GROUP 36 â€” Travel Time & Time-of-Day Overhaul
  Date: April 15, 2026
================================================================================

  PROBLEM STATEMENT
  -----------------
  1. TRAVEL_TIME table was flat by type-pair with no distance awareness.
     'settlementâ†’settlement' = 3 regardless of whether towns are neighbors or
     a continent apart. 'interiorâ†’interior' = 1 â€” walking next door cost hours.
     'settlementâ†’wilderness' = 2 â€” the tree line at the edge of town took half a day.

  2. Clock never advanced during idle play. Only travel or combat moved time.
     Party spending 10 turns shopping experienced zero time passage.

  3. Gate enforcement missing â€” "gates locked at night" existed only as narrative
     text in location features; the engine never enforced it.

  4. Travel intent matching (Issue 14): "I enter the town" could match
     "The Wilds Near Kaara Reach" because word-overlap scored wilderness higher.

  CHANGES MADE
  ------------

      'wildernessâ†’settlement': 1
      'settlementâ†’road': 0         (instant â€” road runs through settlement)
      'roadâ†’settlement': 0
      'roadâ†’road': 1
      'roadâ†’wilderness': 1
      'wildernessâ†’road': 1
      'wildernessâ†’wilderness': 2   (cross-country â€” half a day)

  GROUP 37 â€” Rules Enforcement & NPC Condition Persistence
  Purpose: Phase-1 rerouted from data-file fixes to engine-level rule enforcement.
  Prevent the AI from inventing mechanics (breath weapon KO, phantom items).
  Add NPC condition persistence, non-lethal melee KO, crafted item fields,
  homebrew/crafting prompt rules, and lead-dragonborn subrace guidance.

  PROBLEM BEING SOLVED
  --------------------
  The AI invented two mechanics during play:
    1. Poison breath â†’ knocked NPC unconscious (violates 5e SRD: breath = damage only)
    2. "Dragonborn scale dust" used to revive an unconscious NPC (phantom item, never
       in inventory, never introduced via itemsGained)
  Neither mechanic has any engine or prompt backing. Root fix: add explicit rule
  blocks to all AI prompt paths and engine enforcement in the executor.

  --- PHASE 1 (REROUTED) + PHASE 4 â€” site/src/lib/game/gm-context.ts ---

  buildNarrativeSystemPrompt â€” DISCRETION RULES (YOU MUST NOT):
      Added two new bullets:
      - "Invent breath weapon effects beyond raw damage..."
      - "Reference or hand out consumable items that do not appear in inventory..."

  buildSystemPrompt â€” CRITICAL RULES: Added four new rule sections after QUEST STAKES:

      === BREATH WEAPON & CONDITION RULES ===
      - Breath weapon = damage only, no Poisoned condition, no unconsciousness.
      - POISONED condition = disadvantage on attacks/ability checks ONLY.
      - GRAPPLE = speed 0, does NOT affect saving throws.
      - NPC conditions: use conditionsApplied with NPC id to track.

      === NON-LETHAL DAMAGE ===
      - Engine "Non-lethal KO" mechanic result â†’ target alive, unconscious, 0 HP.
      - Melee only; breath weapons and spells cannot be non-lethal.
      - Do NOT emit npcChanges alive:false for non-lethal KO.

      === CRAFTING & HOMEBREW ITEMS ===
      - No crafting system unless a quest introduces one.
      - Player crafting: 5e downtime baseline (value Ã· 25 GP/day, tool prof required).
      - Crafted items: use crafted:true + craftedFrom fields in itemsGained payload.
      - PHANTOM ITEMS: never reference consumables not in inventory.

      === DRAGONBORN SUBRACES ===
      - "Lead dragonborn" = Green ancestry (15ft cone, CON save, poison damage).
      - DC = 8 + CON mod + prof. Damage: 2d6 (1-5), 3d6 (6-10), 4d6 (11-15), 5d6 (16+).
      - Poison damage does NOT apply Poisoned condition.

  buildStateExtractionPrompt â€” IMPORTANT GUIDELINES: Added three rules:
      - BREATH WEAPON EXTRACTION: never emit conditionsApplied from breath damage.
      - NON-LETHAL KO EXTRACTION: melee KO â†’ emit unconscious, NOT alive:false.
      - PHANTOM ITEMS: do not emit itemsGained for on-the-fly invented items.

  buildNarratorSystemPrompt â€” RULES: Added two bullets:

  GROUP 38 â€” Wilderness False-Positive Travel Bug Fix
  Purpose: Prevent the engine from involuntarily teleporting the player to a
  wilderness exit during normal in-settlement actions.

  PROBLEM BEING SOLVED
  --------------------
  Testing.JSON revealed four involuntary wilderness teleports (turns 5, 10, 12, 15)
  while the player was conducting in-settlement actions at Lordun Ford:
    - "I go and speak with the innkeeper about..."
    - "I walk up to the front desk and ask..."
    - Similar civic/interior actions
  The engine routed all four to "The Wilds Near Lordun Ford" with no player intent.

  ROOT CAUSE
  ----------
  resolveTravel in turn-executor.ts (line ~1836):
      const words = exitLower.split(/\s+/).filter((w) => w.length > 2);
  Word-length threshold of > 2 keeps "the" (3 chars). Every English sentence
  contains "the", so the word "the" in "The Wilds Near Lordun Ford" matched
  every player action, consistently triggering false-positive wilderness travel.

  FIX â€” Three layers, all in resolveTravel (turn-executor.ts)
  -----------------------------------------------------------

  LAYER 1 â€” Word-length threshold + strong-word requirement:
  Changed the matchedExits filter logic from:
      const words = exitLower.split(/\s+/).filter((w) => w.length > 2);
      return words.some((word) => lower.includes(word)) || lower.includes(exitLower);
  To:
      if (lower.includes(exitLower)) return true;  // full name match always qualifies
      const words = exitLower.split(/\s+/).filter((w) => w.length > 3);
      const matchingWords = words.filter((word) => lower.includes(word));
      return matchingWords.length > 0 && matchingWords.some((w) => w.length >= 5);
  Effect: Articles/prepositions (â‰¤ 3 chars: "the", "and", "for") are excluded.
  Short content words (4 chars: "near", "ford", "gate") can contribute to a match
  but are insufficient alone â€” at least one strong word (â‰¥ 5 chars) must match.
  "The Wilds Near Lordun Ford" now requires "wilds"(5) or "lordun"(6) in the action.

  LAYER 2 â€” Wilderness opt-in guard:
  Added after matchedExits is computed:
      const WILDERNESS_OPT_IN = /\b(wilderness|wilds?|wood(s|land)?|forest|outside|
          outskirts|country(side)?|fields?|plains?|leave\s+town|leave\s+cit|
          leave\s+settlement|head\s+out|walk\s+out|ride\s+out|venture\s+out|
          out\s+of\s+town|depart)\b/;
      if (matchedExits.length > 0
          && matchedExits.every((e) => e.type === 'wilderness')
          && !WILDERNESS_OPT_IN.test(lower)) {
          return base;
      }
  Effect: Even if words in a wilderness exit name coincidentally match an action,
  the guard requires explicit wilderness-departure language before allowing the
  travel. In-settlement actions ("walk to the front desk") always return base.
  Wilderness travel ("head into the wilds", "depart", "walk out of town") passes.

  VERIFICATION
  ------------
  Manual trace of the four bug-trigger scenarios:
    "I go and speak with the innkeeper about..." â†’ no strong words from exit â†’ base âœ“
    "I walk up to the front desk and ask..." â†’ no strong words â†’ base; guard also fires âœ“
    "I head into the wilds to gather herbs" â†’ "wilds" (5 chars) passes L1 + L2 opt-in âœ“
    "travel to lordun ford" â†’ full name match "lordun ford" â†’ qualifies âœ“
  npx tsc --noEmit â€” 4 pre-existing errors only, zero new errors.

  FILES MODIFIED
  --------------
  server/ai/turn-executor.ts (resolveTravel function â€” matchedExits filter block)

  GROUP 40 — Jtest5 Audit Fixes: Grapple, Duplicate Guards, Stat Blocks, Gold
  Date: April 16, 2026

  Source: 199-turn Jtest5 session audit (7 issues across 4 phases)
  Files modified: types.ts, creature-templates.ts, turn-executor.ts,
                  adventure-turn.ts, world-enrichment.ts, gm-context.ts

  --- PHASE 1: src/lib/server/ai/turn-executor.ts ---

  [1] Grapple / shove contested check (Issue 5):
      In resolveCombatAttack, after target is resolved and BEFORE weapon
      selection, added GRAPPLE_RE pattern intercept:
        Pattern: /\b(grapple|pin\s+(them|him|her|it|down)|wrestle|
                   grab\s+and\s+hold|tackle|
                   shove\s+(them|him|her|it|down|back|away))\b/i
      When matched inside active combat, returns:
        { ...base, status: 'awaiting-roll', pendingCheck: { kind: 'contested',
          ability: 'str', skill: 'athletics', opposingActorId: target.referenceId,
          combatBound: true }, resolvedActionSummary: reason }
      This bypasses resolveAttack entirely and promotes grapple to a full
      contested check. PendingCheck.kind='contested' and .opposingActorId
      already existed in types.ts (no type changes needed).

  --- PHASE 3: src/lib/server/ai/adventure-turn.ts ---

  [2] Quest gold double-pay dedup in mergeStateChanges (Issues 14 + 21):
      In mergeStateChanges, replaced the simple goldChange merge line with
      an IIFE that filters GM gold entries BEFORE merging:
        - Builds engineQuestRewardKeys: Set of "characterId|delta" for all
          engine goldChange entries whose reason starts with "Quest reward:"
        - Filters gm.goldChange to exclude entries matching those keys
        - Then calls mergeUniqueByKey with the filtered GM array
      Effect: when engine calls distributeQuestRewards (which pushes
      goldChange with reason "Quest reward: ..."), any GM goldChange for
      the same characterId+amount is dropped, preventing double-payment.
      Covers both Issue 14 (verbal promise NPC) and Issue 21 (direct emit).

  [3] NPC name+location duplicate guard in sanitizeStateChanges (Issue 15):
      In the sc.npcsAdded filter, just before return true, added check:
        if state.npcs has any alive NPC with same name (case-insensitive)
        AND same locationId as the incoming NPC → warn + return false.
      Warning: "[sanitize] npcsAdded[N] NPC "X" already exists at
               location "Y" — stripped"

  [4] Flat stat block fill in applyGMStateChanges (Issue 16):
      When constructing the NPC object in the changes.npcsAdded loop
      in applyGMStateChanges, added post-construction logic:
        if (role === 'hostile' || role === 'boss') && isStatBlockFlat(npcData.statBlock):
          tier = role === 'boss' ? 'boss' : 'normal'
          npc.statBlock = generateCreatureStatBlock(name, tier, averagePartyLevel)
        else if npcData.statBlock: npc.statBlock = npcData.statBlock
      Ensures all hostile/boss NPCs added by the GM or AI get scaled,
      archetype-based stat blocks instead of all-10s defaults.
      (isStatBlockFlat and type CreatureTier added to import from
       $lib/game/creature-templates)

  [5] Quest duplicate guard in sanitizeStateChanges (Issue 12):
      In the sc.questsAdded filter, after objectives enforcement,
      added duplicate detection:
        if q.giverNpcId is set:
          compute significant words (length>3, not in STOP_WORDS set) from
          q.name + q.description
          if any existing state.quests entry has same giverNpcId AND shares
          >= 2 significant words → warn + return false
      Warning: "[sanitize] questsAdded[N] "X" duplicates existing quest
               from same giver — stripped"

  --- PHASE 4: src/trigger/world-enrichment.ts ---

  [6] Stat block fill in applyEnrichmentChanges (Issue 16 continued):
      Modified function signature to accept partyLevel = 3 (optional 3rd param).
      Changed NPC push to build a named object (newNpc: NPC) first, then:
        if (role === 'hostile' || role === 'boss') && isStatBlockFlat(statBlock):
          newNpc.statBlock = generateCreatureStatBlock(name, tier, partyLevel)
        else if npcData.statBlock: newNpc.statBlock = npcData.statBlock
      Updated all 3 call sites (expand-settlement, extend-quest-arc,
      react-to-party) to compute and pass:
        averagePartyLevel(state.characters)
      New import added: generateCreatureStatBlock, isStatBlockFlat,
                        averagePartyLevel, type CreatureTier
        from '$lib/game/creature-templates'

  --- PHASE 5: src/lib/game/creature-templates.ts (new export) ---

  [7] Exported isStatBlockFlat helper:
      export function isStatBlockFlat(sb?: CreatureStatBlock): boolean
        Returns true if !sb?.abilities OR all 6 ability scores are falsy
        or equal to 10 (the AI's non-stat default).
      Used by adventure-turn.ts and world-enrichment.ts (Steps 4 + 6).

  --- PHASE 5b: src/lib/game/types.ts (type extension) ---

  [8] Added statBlock?: CreatureStatBlock to StateChange.npcsAdded element:
      Extends the npcsAdded array element type to permit an optional
      statBlock field. This allows the AI to provide stat blocks that are
      then passed through the stat block fill logic (flat ones are replaced).

  --- PHASE 6: src/lib/game/gm-context.ts ---

  [9] buildSystemPrompt — new === ENCOUNTER DECLARATION DISCIPLINE === section
      (Issue 20) — inserted after NON-LETHAL DAMAGE block:
        "NEVER write combat-declaration prose unless stateChanges for THIS
         SAME response include a valid encounterStarted with named creatures.
         Violation creates broken encounter state — UI enters combat mode
         with no combatants."
        "If ACTIVE ENCOUNTER already in state: do NOT re-announce or re-emit
         encounterStarted — fight is already in progress."
        "Scouting, observing, cautious dialogue NEVER warrant combat prose."

  [10] buildSystemPrompt CRITICAL RULES — new QUEST REWARD GOLD rule (Issue 21):
       Inserted after GOLD PAYMENTS rule:
         "Engine automatically distributes quest.rewards.gold when a quest
          completes. NEVER also emit goldChange for that same amount — it
          will be applied twice. Do not narrate NPC paying quest reward AND
          emit goldChange in the same turn."

  [11] buildStateExtractionPrompt IMPORTANT GUIDELINES — two new rules:
       COMBAT PROSE WITHOUT encounterStarted: If narrative contains combat-
         declaration phrases but no encounterStarted was in this turn's
         stateChanges, do NOT retroactively emit encounterStarted.
       QUEST GOLD EXTRACTION: If NPC payment in narrative matches quest
         completion reward in this same turn, do NOT emit goldChange —
         distributeQuestRewards already handles it.

  --- IMPLEMENTATION NOTE ---

  The sanitize-level stat block fill (Step 4) was placed in applyGMStateChanges
  rather than sanitizeStateChanges because StateChange.npcsAdded did not
  originally include a statBlock field. Rather than only extending the type
  (which is also done in Step 8), the generate-on-apply approach guarantees
  the stat block is always set correctly at persistence time, regardless of
  what the AI sends.
